The position of city traffic engineer is hereby authorized. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 1, Article 6,
Section 1-36)
Sec. 10.102 Authority to Erect Traffic Control Devices, Impose Weight Limits†
The city traffic engineer is hereby authorized, on the basis of an engineering and traffic investigation, to erect
and maintain official traffic control devices on any streets or parts of streets to impose gross weight limits. (1988
Seymour City Code, Chapter 19, Article 1, Section 19-1)
Sec. 10.103 Authority to Designate Loading Zones
The city traffic engineer is hereby authorized to determine the location of loading zones and passenger loading
zones and shall place and maintain appropriate signs indicating the same and stating the hours during which
the provisions of this article are applicable. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 19, Article 1, Section 19-2)
Sec. 10.104 Authority to Impose Size Restrictions
The city traffic engineer is hereby authorized, on the basis of an engineering and traffic investigation, to erect
and maintain official traffic control devices on any streets or parts of streets to impose vehicle size restrictions.
(1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 19, Article 1, Section 19-3)
Sec. 10.105 Authority to Exclude Specified Traffic
The city traffic engineer is hereby authorized, on the basis of an engineering and traffic investigation, to
determine and designate those heavily traveled streets upon which shall be prohibited any class or kind of
traffic which is found to be incompatible with the normal and safe movement of traffic and shall erect
appropriate official traffic control devices giving notice thereof. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 19, Article 1,
Section 19-4)
Sec. 10.106 Authority to Impose Truck Restrictions
The city traffic engineer is hereby authorized, on the basis of an engineering and traffic investigation, to erect
and maintain official traffic control devices on any streets or parts of streets to prohibit the operation of trucks
exceeding ten thousand (10,000) pounds gross weight; provided that such devices shall not prohibit necessary
local operation on such streets for the purpose of making a pickup or delivery. (1988 Seymour City Code,
Chapter 19, Article 1, Section 19-5)
Sec. 10.107 Authority to Assign One-Way Streets and Alleys
The city traffic engineer is hereby authorized to determine and designate one-way streets or alleys and shall
place and maintain official traffic control devices giving notice thereof. No such designation shall be effective
unless such devices are in place. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 19, Article 1, Section 19-6)
Sec. 10.108 Authority for Stop Signs and Yield Signs
The city traffic engineer is hereby authorized to erect and maintain stop signs, yield signs, or other official traffic
control devices, to designate through streets or to designate intersections or other roadway junctions at which
vehicular traffic on one or more of the roadways should yield or stop and yield before entering the intersection
or junction. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 19, Article 1, Section 19-7)
Sec. 10.109 Placement of Signs or Markings Indicating Angle Parking
The city traffic engineer shall determine upon what streets angle parking shall be permitted and shall mark or
sign such streets but such angle parking shall not be indicated upon any federal aid or state highway within this
city unless the state highway commission or state highway engineer has determined that the roadway is of
sufficient width to permit angle parking without interfering with the free movement of traffic. (1988 Seymour City
Code, Chapter 19, Article 1, Section 19-8)
Sec. 10.110 Prohibiting Turns at Intersections
The city traffic engineer is hereby authorized to determine those intersections at which drivers of vehicles shall
not make a right, left or U turn, and shall place proper signs at such intersections. The making of such turns

https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 117/221
may be prohibited between certain hours of any day and permitted at other hours, in which event the same
shall be plainly indicated on the signs or they may be removed when such turns are permitted. (1988 Seymour
City Code, Chapter 19, Article 1, Section 19-11)
Sec. 10.111 Authority to Restrict Direction of Movement During Certain Periods
The city traffic engineer is hereby authorized to determine and designate streets, parts of streets, or specific
lanes thereon upon which vehicular traffic shall proceed in one direction during one period and the opposite
direction during another period of the day, and shall place and maintain appropriate markings, signs, barriers or
other devices to give notice thereof. The city traffic engineer may erect signs temporarily designating lanes to
be used by traffic moving in a particular direction, regardless of the center line of the roadway. (1988 Seymour
City Code, Chapter 19, Article 1, Section 19-12)
Sec. 10.112 Powers of and Appointment of Traffic Engineer
The city secretary shall have all powers and duties of the traffic engineer until such time as the council shall hire
a traffic engineer. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 19, Article 1, Section 19-13)
Sec. 10.113 No U-Turn Signs
It shall be unlawful for any person to make a u-turn between the north end of 300 Block of Washington Street
and shall extend to the south end of the 100 Block of Washington Street.
(1) Performing a 180-degree rotation to reverse the direction of travel.
(2) Turning across a lane of travel marked or unmarked for the purpose of parking.
(3) Exception. Vehicle needing to operate in a manner to make immediate delivery to place of
business in zoned area.
(Ordinance 2012-04 adopted 3/22/12)
ARTICLE 10.200 GENERAL TRAFFIC REGULATIONS
Sec. 10.201 State Speed Laws Applicable
The state traffic laws regulating the speed of vehicles shall be applicable upon all streets within this city except
where the city traffic engineer, on the basis of an engineering and traffic investigation, determines that other
speed limits shall be applicable on specified streets or in certain areas, in which event it shall be unlawful for
any person to drive a vehicle at a speed in excess of any speed so determined when signs are in place giving
notice thereof. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 19, Article 2, Section 19-14)
Sec. 10.202 Duty of Officers to Enforce Traffic Laws
It shall be the duty of the officers of the police department or such officers as are assigned by the police to
enforce all street traffic laws of this city and all of the state vehicle laws applicable to street traffic in this city.
(1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 19, Article 2, Section 19-15)
Sec. 10.203 Authority of Police Officers to Direct Traffic
Officers of the police department or such officers as are assigned by the chief of police are hereby authorized to
direct all traffic by voice, hand or signal in conformance with traffic laws, providing that in the event of a fire or
other emergency or to expedite traffic or to safeguard pedestrians, officers of the police department may direct
traffic as conditions may require notwithstanding the provisions of the traffic laws. (1988 Seymour City Code,
Chapter 19, Article 2, Section 19-16)
Sec. 10.204 Emergency and Experimental Regulations
The chief of police may authorize the temporary placing of official traffic control devices when required by an
emergency. The chief of police shall notify the city traffic engineer of his action as soon thereafter as is
practicable. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 19, Article 2, Section 19-17)
Sec. 10.205 Display of Unauthorized Signs, Signals or Markings
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 118/221
(a) No person shall place, maintain or display upon or in view of any highway any unauthorized sign, signal,
markings, or device which purports to be or is an imitation of or resembles an official traffic-control device or
railroad sign or signal, or which attempts to direct the movement of traffic, or which hides from view or interferes
with the effectiveness of any official traffic control device or any railroad sign or signal.
(b) No person shall place or maintain nor shall any public authority permit upon any highway any sign or
signal bearing thereon any commercial advertising. No person shall place or maintain a sign across or above a
street unless permission is granted by the city traffic engineer.
(c) This section shall not be deemed to prohibit the erection upon private property adjacent to a highway of
signs giving useful directional information and of a type that cannot be mistaken for official signs.
(d) Every such prohibited sign, signal or marking is hereby declared a public nuisance and the authority
having jurisdiction of the highway is hereby empowered to remove the same or cause it to be removed without
notice.
(1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 19, Article 2, Section 19-18)
Sec. 10.206 Interfering with Devices, Signs or Signals
No person shall without lawful authority attempt to or in fact alter, deface, injure, knock down, or remove any
official traffic control device or any railroad sign or signal or any inscription, shield or insignia thereon, or any
other part thereof. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 19, Article 2, Section 19-19)
State law reference–Destruction of traffic–control devices, Vernon's Ann. Civ. Stat., art. 6701d, section 37.
Sec. 10.207 Use of Streets to Sell Vehicles Unlawful
It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to use any portion of any public street, alley, avenue or
highway in the city as a stand for the sale or offering for sale or trade of any automobile, automobile truck,
motorcycle or other vehicle of any description, motor or otherwise, or to use any portion of any public street,
alley, avenue or highway for the purpose of sale or offering for sale or trade of any automobile, automobile
truck, motorcycle or other vehicle, motor or otherwise, by parking said vehicle or running same upon the streets
of the city with a “For Sale” or other sign upon them, indicating that such vehicles are for sale. (1988 Seymour
City Code, Chapter 19, Article 2, Section 19-20)
Sec. 10.208 Full Stop Required at Stop Signs
Any motor driven or other vehicle operation upon a public street, alley or other public way, shall come to a full
stop where such stop signs are installed and maintained by the city. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 19,
Article 2, Section 19-21)
Sec. 10.209 Vehicle Operators, Pedestrians to Obey Traffic Signals
It shall hereafter be unlawful for any person to operate any vehicle or attempt to operate any vehicle, or for any
pedestrian to walk, or attempt to walk, into or across the intersection of Washington and McLain Streets in the
city, when the red or amber lights are displayed facing or opposing the direction of said vehicle or pedestrian;
and it shall be the duty of every person operating a vehicle, upon approaching such street intersection, or when
such vehicle is standing at or near such intersection, to promptly proceed in the same direction across the
intersection, and pedestrians may proceed in the same direction across such intersection, upon the appearance
of the green light facing and opposing the direction of such vehicle or pedestrian; provided, that any vehicle
may turn from its original course to the left into the intersecting street, only upon the display of the green light
facing or opposing the original course of such vehicle. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 19, Article 2, Section
19-22)
Sec. 10.210 Pedestrians to Have Right-of-Way; Conditions
Pedestrians shall have the right-of-way when proceeding across any such intersection upon the display of the
green light facing and opposing the direction of such pedestrians, over all vehicles which may turn to the right
after entering such intersections for the purpose of proceeding along the intersecting street, and over all
vehicles no matter in what direction such vehicles may be proceeding. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 19,
Article 2, Section 19-23)
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 119/221
Sec. 10.211 Intersection Defined
The term “intersection” as used in this article shall, when applied to the operation of vehicles, mean that area at
the crossing of such street that is embraced within lines projected at right angles to and across said streets
from property line to property line, and when applied to the movement of pedestrians, same shall mean all of
said area except the sidewalks therein. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 19, Article 2, Section 19-24)
Sec. 10.212 Vehicle Defined
The term “vehicle” as used in this article, shall mean all motor driven vehicles, horse-drawn vehicles, bicycles,
and all other means of travel other than by foot. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 19, Article 2, Section 19-
25)
Sec. 10.213 Neighborhood Electric Vehicles, Motorized Neighborhood Vehicles or Motor-Assisted
Scooters
(a) In the interest of public safety, the use of neighborhood electric vehicles, neighborhood motorized
vehicles or motor-assisted scooters, is prohibited on the streets, highways, alleys and public paths in the city.
(b) The Code of Ordinances of the city, shall prohibit the operation of the use of neighborhood electric
vehicles, neighborhood motorized vehicles or motor-assisted scooters, in the city, and the Code of Ordinances
of the city, shall include the following section to read verbatim as follows:
(1) For purposes of this section the terms “neighborhood electric vehicles” and “motor-assisted
scooter” shall have the same meaning assigned by Transportation Code, section 551.301, as
amended. A “motorized neighborhood vehicle” is defined as the same as a “neighborhood electric
vehicle” but utilizing a gas or other fossil fuel powered motor.
(2) A person may not operate a neighborhood electric vehicle or motorized neighborhood vehicle
or motor-assisted scooter, which travels at speeds of 2 miles per hour or greater, with the exception
of scooters for the disabled, electric wheelchairs designed to assist physically disabled persons and
properly licensed and insured motorized vehicles, on any alley, street or highway within the city.
(3) It shall be unlawful for any person to ride, drive or park any neighborhood electric vehicle,
neighborhood motorized vehicle or motor-assisted scooter, over or across any public park, curb,
sidewalk, grass, lawn, hiking or jogging trail, path or park land within the city. This section is not
applicable to municipal vehicles.
(Ordinance 2005-10 adopted 5/19/05)
Sec. 10.214 Engine Retarding Devices
(a) No person shall operate an engine of any motor vehicle so as to “brake” or slow the same through the
use of gears (commonly known as “jake braking”) or by any other method which produces any noise in addition
to the normal operating engine noise, within the city limits.
(b) Any person, firm, or corporation violating any of the provisions or terms of this section shall be guilty of a
misdemeanor and upon conviction, shall be fined a sum not to exceed $500.00 for each offense, and each and
every violation or day such violation shall continue or exist, shall be deemed a separate offense.
(Ordinance 2004-05 adopted 7/15/04)
Sec. 10.215 Golf Carts and Utility Vehicles
(a) Golf carts shall be defined (per Texas Transportation Code section 502.401 item 18) as vehicles designed
to operate at a maximum speed of 25 miles per hour or less and excludes all-terrain vehicles and design
altered golf carts, and slow moving vehicles.
(b) The following regulations and requirements shall apply to all golf carts and other slow moving vehicles on
public streets in the city.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 120/221
(1) Each operator of a golf cart shall maintain financial responsibility (insurance) as required of
other passenger vehicles in the Texas Transportation Code section 601.051.
(2) Golf can operators must have a valid driver's license as required of other passenger vehicles
in the Texas Transportation Code title 7, subchapter B, section 521.021.
(3) Golf carts will be operated during daylight hours only.
(4) Golf carts will only be operated on roadways where posted speed limits do not exceed 35
miles per hour.
(5) Golf carts shall display a “slow-moving vehicle” emblem that has a reflective surface designed
to be clearly visible in daylight and shall be maintained in a clean, reflective condition.
(6) Golf carts shall be equipped with front and rear lamps, an exterior mirror mounted on the
driver's side of the vehicle and either an exterior mirror mounted on the passenger side of the
vehicle or an interior mirror, a parking brake, reflex reflectors (1 red on each side as far to the rear as
practicable and 1 red on the rear).
(7) Operators of golf carts shall not allow anyone to sit in the lap of the operator or passengers of
the vehicle, nor allow anyone to stand up in the vehicle during the operation of the vehicle.
Passengers shall be limited to seating capacity as designed by the manufacturer.
(8) Golf carts shall not be operated on city sidewalks or pathways.
(9) Golf carts shall yield the right-of-way to other vehicles when traveling.
(10) All-terrain vehicles are prohibited from operating on all public streets.
(11) Design altered golf carts that have been altered to allow them to travel at a speed greater
than 25 miles per hour are prohibited from operating on all public streets.
(12) Golf carts are prohibited from pulling trailers, boats, jet skis, etc.
(c) Any person, firm, corporation or other entity that violates the terms of the above referenced regulations
and requirements, or other terms of this section shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor punishable by a fine
not to exceed $500.00.
(Ordinance 2016-05 adopted 5/26/16)
ARTICLE 10.300 PARKING*
Sec. 10.301 Parallel Parking Zone Designated
North Main Street, being all of Main Street north of Ingram Street, is hereby designated a street for parallel
parking of motor vehicles only so that any person parking a motor vehicle of any description, or any other type
of conveyance or self-propelled vehicle or machine, on North Main Street aforesaid, shall park said vehicle
inside the parallel parking area marked off on the street so that the vehicle when parked shall be near to and
parallel to the curb and inside the parking area designated, so that said motor vehicle shall not be parked
across any parking lines either to the side, front or back of the vehicle. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 19,
Article 3, Section 19-31)
Sec. 10.302 Ten Minute Zone Designated
There is hereby created a ten (10) minute parking limit on the east street vehicle parking right-of-way of North
Washington Street abutting Lots 1-9, Block 19, Original Town Addition. The aforementioned parking limit shall
be construed to mean that any vehicle, either engine-powered or self-propelled, shall not park in the
aforementioned parking right-of-way for a period exceeding ten (10) minutes at one interval. (1988 Seymour
City Code, Chapter 19, Article 3, Section 19-45)
Sec. 10.303 Overnight “No Parking” Zones Designated; Exceptions

It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to obstruct any portion of any public street, alley, avenue
or highway in the city by placing, parking or leaving thereon any type of vehicle, tractor, trailer, motorcycle,
farming equipment or any other type of self-propelled device, during the hours of 8:00 a.m. to 6:00 p.m., unless

Sec. 10.305 School No Parking Zones Designated; School Areas
(a) There is hereby created a “No Parking” zone on the north street parking right-of-way of East California
Street, abutting the south side of Block 6, McLain Addition. The aforementioned “No Parking” zone shall be
construed to mean that any vehicle shall not park in the aforementioned right-of-way between the hours of 8:00
a.m. and 4:00 p.m. on days during which the elementary school is in operation.
(b) There is hereby created a “No Parking” zone on the east street parking right-of-way of North East Street
abutting the west side of Block 11, McLain Addition. The aforementioned “No Parking” zone shall be construed
to mean that any vehicle shall not park in the aforementioned parking right-of-way at any time during school
days and hours of operation, except those vehicles bearing Texas exempt license tags.
(c) There is hereby created a “No Parking” zone on the east street parking right-of-way of North East Street
abutting the west side of Block 11, McLain Addition. The aforementioned “No Parking” zone shall be construed
to mean that any vehicle shall not park in the aforementioned parking right-of-way at any time during school
days and hours of operation, except those vehicles authorized in conjunction with operations of the Seymour
Independent School District.
(1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 19, Article 3, Section 19-51)
Sec. 10.306 Additional “No Parking” Zones Established
A “no parking” zone shall be established on the hereinafter described highways:
(1) On either side of U.S. 183, U.S. 277, and U.S. 283 from the south side of Clay Street to the
east side of Cedar Street.
(2) On the south street parking right-of-way of East Morris Street abutting the east eighty (80) feet
of the north side of Lot 1, Block 5, Original Town Addition. The aforementioned zone shall be
construed to mean that any vehicle shall not park in the aforementioned parking right-of-way, at any
time, except those vehicles authorized in conjunction with the storage facilities located on Lot 1,
Block 5, Original Town Addition.
(3) On West California Street extending from North Main Street west to the city limits line.
(4) On Ingram Street from South Main Street extending east to the city limits line.
(5) Beginning at the intersection of North Main and Nevada Streets, extending east on Nevada
Street to its east end, and continuing on east on Ellis Street to its intersection with Stadium Drive,
and continuing on Stadium Drive (formerly Kerr Street) to its intersection with the corporate city limits
line.

Sec. 10.307 Parking Within Fire Zone Limited
It shall hereafter be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to obstruct any portion of any public street,
alley, avenue or highway in the city by placing, parking or leaving any type of vehicle or trailer thereon, which is
within the boundaries of the city fire zone, continuously for a period of twenty-four (24) hours or more. (1988
Seymour City Code, Chapter 19, Article 3, Section 19-62)
Sec. 10.308 Double Parking Unlawful
Double parking is absolutely prohibited, except that parties in an automobile may stop behind cars for the
purpose of getting service from stores and shops, provided someone capable of operating such vehicle is left at
the wheel. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 19, Article 3, Section 19-63)
Sec. 10.309 Unlawful to Park Near Fireplug
It shall be unlawful to park a car within fifteen (15) feet of any fireplug within the city. (1988 Seymour City Code,
Chapter 19, Article 3, Section 19-64)
Sec. 10.310 Thirty Minute Zone Designated
(a) There is hereby created a thirty (30) minute parking limit on the west street vehicle parking right-of-way of
South Washington Street abutting lots 17-21, Block 8, Original Town Addition of the City of Seymour. The
aforementioned parking limit shall be construed to mean that any vehicle, either engine-powered or selfpropelled,
shall not park in the aforementioned parking tight-of-way, for a period exceeding thirty (30) minutes at
one interval.
(b) There is hereby created a thirty (30) minute parking limit at the aforementioned location for three (3)
parking spaces, only. Thirty (30) minute parking signs shall be erected at the aforementioned location.
(c) Any vehicle, either engine powered or self-propelled, found parking in the aforementioned parking area an
interval longer than thirty (30) minutes, as mentioned in subsection (a), shall be issued a citation by a law
enforcement official of the City of Seymour.
(Ordinance 92-4 adopted 6/11/92)
ARTICLE 10.400 LOADING ZONES
Sec. 10.401 Permits for Loading or Unloading at Angle to Curb
The city traffic engineer is authorized to issue special permits to authorize the backing of a vehicle to the curb
for the purpose of loading or unloading property subject to the terms and conditions of such permit. Such
permits may be issued either to the owner or lessee of real property alongside the curb or to the owner of the
vehicle and shall grant to such person the privilege as therein stated and herein authorized. (1988 Seymour
City Code, Chapter 19, Article 1, Section 19-9)
Sec. 10.402 Standing in Loading Zones
(a) No person shall stop, stand or park a vehicle for any purpose or length of time other than for the
expeditious unloading and delivery or pick-up and loading of property in any place marked as a loading zone
during hours when the provisions applicable to such zones are in effect. In no case shall the stop for loading
and unloading of property exceed thirty (30) minutes.
(b) The driver of a vehicle may stop temporarily at a loading zone for the purpose of and while actually
engaged in loading or unloading passengers when such stopping does not interfere with any vehicle which is
waiting to enter or about to enter such zone to load or unload property.
(1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 19, Article 1, Section 19-10)
ARTICLE 10.500 TRUCK ROUTES
Sec. 10.501 Routes Designated
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 123/221
No truck with a payload rating of more than 5,000 pounds may drive upon any public street within the corporate
city limits with the following exceptions:
(1) Said trucks may use U.S. and state designated thoroughfares including State Farm Roads 422
and 1919.
(2) Said trucks may use Oregon Street, Nevada Street, and Idaho Street between Cedar and
Main Street (U.S. 283-182-277).
(3) Said trucks may use Cedar Street and Oak Street between California Street (U.S. 82) and
Oregon Street.
(4) Said trucks may use any other road, street or thoroughfare located within the corporate limits
of the city when traveling directly to or from the drivers residence providing said truck and/or trailer
will be parked on an all-weather surface, when in route to deliver or to pick up cargo, but only when
the destination for delivery or pickup cannot be accessed by utilizing any of the above named roads,
streets or thoroughfares. In such instances said trucks may use only the most direct route in going to
or coming from the location at which it is to deliver or pick up cargo. Said trucks are also allowed to
pick up fuel at the location of their choice providing they take the most direct route to or from any of
the above named roads, streets or thoroughfares.
(5) Emergency vehicles, city vehicles, commercial trash haulers, school buses and commercial
harvesters traveling to the city for the sole purpose of performing seasonal work are exempted from
this section.
Sec. 10.502 Leaving Truck Unattended
It shall be unlawful to leave either an unattended truck, truck tractor, or a tractor trailer parked on any of the city
streets, thoroughfares or alleyways within the corporate limits of the city, at any time. Any of such vehicles
remaining parked unattended upon the streets, thoroughfares or alleyways of this city for more than three (3)
hours shall be prima facie evidence of a violation of this section.
Sec. 10.503 Penalty for Violations
Any person, firm, or corporation violating the provisions of this article shall be deemed guilty of a separate
offense for each day* or portion of a day* during which any violation hereof shall be committed and conviction
of any such violation shall be held punishable by a fine of not less than twenty-five ($165.00) [sic] nor more
than two hundred dollars ($500.00).
* (Day begins at 12:01 a.m. and ends at 12:00 p.m. midnight.)
(Ordinance 2018-09 adopted 11/15/18)

ARTICLE 10.800 TRAFFIC HAZARDS ABATEMENT
Sec. 10.801 Abatement of Tree, Shrub, etc. Traffic Hazards Authorized
Whenever the city secretary or street superintendent of the city shall find a tree, hedge, scrub or other natural
growth of any kind or description, located and growing within the boundaries of any public street in the city,
which interferes with the vision of any motorist or driver while driving upon such streets, thereby constituting a
traffic hazard, the city secretary or street superintendent is therefore authorized and directed to abate the traffic
hazard by trimming or removing any such obstruction. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 19, Article 8, Section
19-91)
Sec. 10.802 Notice to Owner
The city secretary is hereby instructed to give notice to the owner of any abutting property and afford such
owner the opportunity to do the work of removing said traffic hazard, but shall not be required to await the
owner's action in any case where he shall find that the public safety requires the immediate abatement of such
hazard. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 19, Article 8, Section 19-92)
Sec. 10.803 Abatement by City
In all cases where immediate action is not required, a notice shall be sent to the owner of an abutting property
stating that the hazard needs to be removed in the interest of public safety. If the same has not been removed
within ten (10) days of the notice, the work will be done by the city and the expenses incurred shall be billed to
the owner. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 19, Article 8, Section 19-93)
Sec. 10.804 Appeal
In the event that any interested person is dissatisfied with the action of the city secretary, he may, within the ten
(10) day period of notice hereinabove described, file and appeal the matter in the city council whose judgment
thereon shall be final. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 19, Article 8, Section 19-94)
Sec. 10.805 Vision Requirements
On any corner lot or parkway adjacent thereto, a fence, wall, sign, hedge, tree or obstruction of any nature
erected, planted or maintained so as to interfere with sight lines at elevations between two (2) and eight (8) feet
above the top of the adjacent roadway curb, or if there is no curb, then from the average street grade, within a
triangular area formed by the intersection of the adjacent curb lines, or if none exists, the normal curb lines and
a point on each curb line forty-five (45) feet from the intersection, shall be prima facie evidence that such fence,
wall, sign, hedge, tree or obstruction of any nature constitutes an obstruction to vision as it regards public safety
on the streets. The triangular area of visibility as provided for herein is further described and depicted in the
drawing as maintained on file in the office of the city secretary. Any such fence, wall, sign, hedge, tree or
obstruction of any nature erected, planted or maintained in violation of this article shall be removed upon written
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 130/221
notice from the city secretary served upon the owner or occupant of the premises where such obstruction has
been erected, planted or maintained. In the event the obstruction is not removed within ten (10) days after
notice, it may be removed by the city at the expense of the property owner. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter
19, Article 8, Section 19-95)
ARTICLE 10.900 TRAIN SPEED AND OTHER REGULATIONS
(a) Train Speed Limit Set. It shall be unlawful for any engineer or other person in charge of any electric,
gasoline motor or steam locomotive or train to run the same within the corporate limits of the city at a greater
rate of speed than ten (10) miles per hour. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 19, Article 9, Section 19-101)
(b) Flagman or Automatic Signals Required at Crossings. Each railroad company having a track or tracks
crossing the State Highway in the city at the following places: Oak Street where the same intersects California
Street; Washington Street where the same is crossed with the Railway Company, shall have and is hereby
required to keep a flagman at said crossings to give notice of the approach of trains, engines and cars upon
said tracks. It is to be construed that the flagman shall not remain on constant duty but shall be on duty only
when trains, engines or cars are actually approaching the crossing. In lieu of the flagman required, said railway
company may install automatic grade crossing gates or may provide other automatic signaling devices,
provided, however, that such automatic gates or other signaling devices shall be approved by the city council
before their installation. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 19, Article 9, Section 19-102)
CHAPTER 11
UTILITIES & SOLID WASTE*
ARTICLE 11.100 GARBAGE AND OTHER REFUSE
Sec. 11.101 City Service for Residences
The owner, occupant or lessee of every residence within the city shall be required to place all garbage and
trash in receptacles placed by the contractor in the alley or adjacent to the street. Said owner, occupant or
lessee shall be billed at the rates established in Section 11.106, as long as such residence is occupied or city
water and/or electrical service is intact.
Sec. 11.102 City Service for Commercial Establishments
The owner, occupant or lessee of every residence within the city shall be required to place all garbage and
trash in receptacles placed by the contractor in the alley or adjacent to the street. Said owner, occupant or
lessee shall be billed at the rates established in Section 11.106, as long as such residence is occupied or city
water and/or electrical service is intact.
Sec. 11.103 Residents Out of City Limits/County Residents
Residents living outside the city limits may:
(1) Transport their own refuse to the transfer station at rate listed in Section 11.106.
(2) Have their refuse collected at the outside city limit rate, if contractor deems the point of
collection is feasible.
Sec. 11.104 Commercial Out of City Limits/County Residents
Commercial customers within the extra territorial jurisdiction of ½ mile outside the city limits will be charged the
inside the city limit commercial rate. Commercial businesses outside this boundary will be charged as listed in
Section 11.106.
Sec. 11.105 Transfer Station
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 131/221
(a) In General.
(1) The transfer station will assess all subscribers and non-subscribers a fee for disposal of
garbage and brush at the rates established in Section 11.106 of this article. A subscriber is a
monthly fee payer whether residential or commercial inside or outside the city limits. A nonsubscriber
is anyone not currently paying monthly fees and will pay for services at the gate or at city
hall, at rates established in Section 11.106.
(2) According to state rules, all vehicles with open beds must be tarped or covered in some
manner to prevent refuse from blowing out. Trailers, pickup trucks and trucks must have side boards
and tailgates with no trash visible, otherwise the load must be tarped or secured with tie downs.
Loads not in compliance will be denied admittance to the facility.
(b) Refuse Prohibited at Transfer Station. The following waste materials will not be accepted at the solid
waste transfer station by residential customers, commercial establishments, contractors or haulers:
(1) Rock or large concrete debris.
(2) Tires.
Disposal of these materials will be the responsibility of said residential customer or commercial operator to
coordinate with the private waste collection contractor by using rentable containers/roll offs at construction work
site.
(Ordinance 2000-06 adopted 8/17/00)
(c) Hours of Operation for the Solid Waste Transfer Station. The hours of operation for the solid waste
transfer station are hereby established:
Summer (March–November) Winter (December–February)
Tuesday–Friday 2:00 p.m.–6:00 p.m. 1:00 p.m.–5:00 p.m.
Saturday 9:00 a.m.–5:00 p.m. 9:00 a.m.–5:00 p.m.
Sunday Closed
Monday Closed
Holidays Closed
(Ordinance 2014-07 adopted 8/21/14)
Sec. 11.106 Rates
Garbage collection rates shall be as provided for in the fee schedule found in the appendix of this code.
(Ordinance 2000-11 adopted 12/14/00)
Sec. 11.107 Burning of Garbage, etc.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 132/221
(a) It is hereby prohibited for any person to burn garbage, trash, debris, structures, or other related articles
within the city limits, save and except the volunteer fire department of the city may, without violating this article,
burn structures solely for the purpose of training volunteer fire fighters. The volunteer fire department must
obtain authorization from TNRCC prior to conducting outdoor burning for training.
(b) Violation of this article shall be punishable by a fine in accordance with the general penalty provision
found in Section 1.106 of this code.
(Ordinance 99-08 adopted 6/17/99)
Sec. 11.108 Sanitation Service Charges Payable; Discontinuance of Utility Service for Nonpayment
(a) There is hereby provided a penalty for those parties failing to pay their monthly utility bill when such bill is
due. It shall be the duty of the city utility billing department to notify each resident user and bill them for
sanitation service each month with their water bill and said bill shall be due on the first (1st) day of each month
and payable in the same manner as the water bills are paid.
(b) The City of Seymour, at its option, may suspend or terminate any or all utility services to include
electricity, water and sewer services of the owner, occupant or lessee of every residence within the City of
Seymour and of the owner, occupant or lessee of every commercial establishment within the City of Seymour
who shall fail to pay the prescribed charges assessed against them as herein provided for sanitation pickup.
(1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 11, Article 1, Section 11-5; Ordinance 94-11 adopted 11/17/94)
Sec. 11.109 Collection Schedule
Garbage and refuse situated at residences shall be picked up twice per week. Services rendered to commercial
and industrial areas shall be as needed. Boardinghouses, even though operated in a private home, shall be
placed in the commercial category. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 11, Article 1, Section 11-7)
Sec. 11.110 City Not to Collect if Article is Violated
The city will not make collection of any garbage, trash or rubbish or tree limbs where same is not prepared for
collection and placed as designated by the terms of this article. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 11, Article
1, Section 11-8)
Sec. 11.111 Disposal of Rock, Waste, Building Debris and Other Trash
Rock, waste, building materials or other trash resulting from construction or remodeling or from a general cleanup
of vacant or improved property or from sizable amounts of trees, trash or debris cleaned from property will
not be removed by the city as a regular service but may be done for the owner for payment of an extra fee.
Exceptions to this section will be made during any clean-up campaign which is proclaimed and authorized by
the mayor or city council. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 11, Article 1, Section 11-9)
Sec. 11.112 Disposal of Animal Waste
Manure from private stables, cow lots, poultry yards, pigeon lofts, or refuse from animals or night soil and dead
animals, and all waste not herein mentioned, must be kept in a separate suitable container and not dumped in
the alleys or retained on the premises to become a nuisance. It shall be disposed of by the occupant of the
premises at his own expense. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 11, Article 1, Section 11-10)
Sec. 11.113 Removal of Dead Animals
The owner or possessor of any animal which may die within the city limits shall within twenty-four (24) hours
after death of such animal, cause the carcass to be removed beyond the city limits at his own expense.
Exceptions to this section may be made in case of dogs and cats and other small house pets which may be
removed by the city. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 11, Article 1, Section 11-11)
Sec. 11.114 Unlawful to Dump Heavy Animals on City Property; Penalty
Heavy dead animals shall include livestock such as cattle, horses, mules, donkeys, goats, sheep, hogs and any
type of animal generally classified as a heavy animal. Henceforth, it shall be a violation of this article for anyone
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 133/221
to deliver or to cause to be delivered any such dead animal as herein defined onto the city dump grounds or
any city-owned property. Any person, firm or corporation violating any of the provisions of this section shall be
deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction shall be fined in accordance with the general penalty
provision found in Section 1.106 of this code. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 11, Article 1, Section 11-12)
Sec. 11.115 Deposits on Streets or Alleys Prohibited
The placing of kitchen garbage, trash or rubbish or material in any street or alley within the city limits is
prohibited. Any owner, occupant or leasee found to be in violation of this section shall be subject to a fine in
accordance with the general penalty provision found in Section 1.106 of this code. (1988 Seymour City Code,
Chapter 11, Article 1, Section 11-13)
Sec. 11.116 Fines
Any person, firm or corporation violating any of the provisions of this article shall be deemed guilty of a
misdemeanor and upon conviction, shall be subject to a fine in accordance with the general penalty provision
found in Section 1.106 of this code. (Ordinance 2000-06 adopted 8/17/00)
ARTICLE 11.200 LANDFILL REGULATIONS
Sec. 11.201 Approved Manner of Disposal
All garbage, rubbish, trash or other solid waste material must be disposed of in a manner approved by the City
of Seymour and its authorized representatives. (Ordinance 88-18 adopted 10/13/88)
Sec. 11.202 Permit Required
Effective as of the date of this article, no person except employees of the City of Seymour or duly authorized
agents, shall empty garbage or trash from any vehicle into the landfill unless such person has obtained a permit
or license, or is otherwise authorized by this article or has paid the specified charges for entry into the landfill. It
shall be unlawful for any attendant at the landfill or any person to dump trash or garbage in the landfill unless
said person has a permit or license to dump or has paid a specified charge for dumping. (Ordinance 88-18
adopted 10/13/88, Section 1)
Sec. 11.203 Rates
(a) There shall be charged and collected for the permission to use and the use of the City of Seymour
Landfill, the amounts as set forth below:
(b) Persons who pay regular monthly residential garbage rates to the city may receive a free landfill permit
sticker which shall be good for one (1) year. Permits will expire December 31 regardless of date of issuance.
When exhibited properly attached on the front of a pickup truck, car or car-pulled trailer, a current and valid
sticker will allow them to dump refuse hauled from their personal residence in accordance with charges set out
below. This sticker may not be used for vehicles larger than the aforementioned, regardless of (the operator's)
residency with the city.
(c) The permit must be obtained at the city hall or at the landfill prior to the vehicle entering the city landfill.
The city reserves the right to deny a permit to any person, when determined to be in the best interest of the city.
(d) All holders of landfill stickers or permits will furnish, upon request of the landfill attendant, the address
from which the refuse was removed. Persons who are found to be in violation of their landfill sticker or permit
will have their permit revoked and be barred from further entrance to the landfill and assessed a fine as
provided in Section 11.216, each violation will constitute a separate and punishable offense.
(e) No junk, wrecked, dismantled or abandoned vehicles will be allowed to be disposed of in the landfill.
(Ordinance 92-12 adopted 9/10/92, Section 2)
Sec. 11.204 Annual Permit Fee
The city shall furnish permit stickers for windshield display as provided for in the fee schedule found in the
appendix of this code. (Ordinance 92-12 adopted 9/10/92, Section 2)
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 134/221
Sec. 11.205 Landfill Charges
Landfill charges shall be as provided for in the fee schedule found in the appendix of this code. (Ordinance 92-
12 adopted 9/10/92, Section 2)
Sec. 11.206 Annual Permits/Licenses Not Transferable
Permit or License Holders may not allow other parties to use their Permits/Licenses, and Permits/Licenses are
not transferable. (Ordinance 92-12 adopted 9/10/92, Section 2.1)
Sec. 11.207 Dumping Procedures
It shall be unlawful for any attendant at a landfill or landfills owned or maintained by the city or any other
employee of the city to allow or permit any such person to dump garbage or trash in a city landfill from a vehicle
unless such vehicle is licenses hereunder or has valid Permit Sticker attached to windshield. After
determination of validity of License or Permit, the attendant at the landfill shall note thereto the city license
number, the current state registration number, and the make and model of the vehicle and licenses or permit
number. Upon receipt of cash for dumping, the attendant shall make out in triplicate a ticket noting thereon the
current registration number and the make and model of the vehicle, and shall give one copy to the person
desiring to dump said garbage or trash, one copy shall remain in the book, and one copy is to be transmitted to
the city office. At the close of each day, all cash collected shall be transmitted to the designated depository.
(Ordinance 92-12 adopted 9/10/92, Section 2.2)
Sec. 11.208 Procedures for Current Holders of Landfill Permits
Commercial Operators and Holders of current Landfill Permits may receive credit toward new annual permit for
unused portion of permit. Basis for credit will be prorated at the rate of 8% per month for each month remaining
on permit. (Ordinance 92-12 adopted 9/10/92, Section 2.3)
Sec. 11.209 Use of City Service Required
All residence and business in the city limits are required to be on city sanitation services and pay the
appropriate fee. city residents and businesses pay for sanitation services, including container pick-up by the
City Sanitation Department. It shall be unlawful for County residents and businesses to empty garbage and
trash in containers provided for those residents and businesses paying for sanitation pick-up service, and
violators will be subject to penalties set out in Section 11.216. (Ordinance 92-12 adopted 9/10/92, Section 3)
Sec. 11.210 Landfill Available to Persons Outside City Limits
The landfill is owned and operated entirely for the citizens of the City of Seymour and residents and businesses
operating outside the city limits of Seymour will be allowed to dump at the landfill site in accordance with
License/Permit fees set out in Section 11.204.
(Ordinance 92-12 adopted 9/10/92, Section 4)
Sec. 11.211 Disclaimer of City Liability
Any person entering the city operated disposal site for any reason shall be conclusively presumed to know the
hazards and the extent of the damage which accompanies the disposal of solid waste materials and the use of
trucks, vehicles and heavy machinery to move, remove, bury and dispose of same and by his or her actions in
entering upon such site and for and in consideration of the permission granted by the city to enter upon such
site, every person shall covenant and be deemed to have covenanted not to sue and to indemnify, save
harmless and defend the city, its agents, officers and employees from and against any and all claims of any
nature whatsoever for injury or damage to person or property, whether real or asserted, arising out of or
resulting from the entry by such person upon the city-operated disposal site. (Ordinance 88-18, adopted
10/13/88, Section 5)
Sec. 11.212 Disposal of Solid Waste Materials
(a) It shall be unlawful for any person to take, remove, or carry away from the city operated disposal site any
garbage, rubbish, trash or other solid waste material, whether or not same has monetary value, without prior
written approval of the city secretary.

https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 135/221
(b) The city secretary shall have the authority to curtail, temporarily suspend, or permanently halt any solid
waste disposal operation conducted by any private person, firm or corporation which does not conform to the
requirements of city, county or state regulations pertaining thereto or shall in any manner jeopardize the public
health, safety and welfare.
(Ordinance 88-18, adopted 10/13/88, Section 6)
Sec. 11.213 Reserved*
Sec. 11.214 Specifying Charges for Disposal of Solid Waste
Governmental agencies and schools hauling their own waste may, after obtaining annual commercial
license/permit, may be billed on a monthly basis for number and size of loads from the attendant's dumping
receipt book, payable on each agency's statements. (Ordinance 92-12, adopted 9/10/92, Section 8)
Sec. 11.215 Specifying Charges for Disposal of City Flat Bed Truck Loads
Flat bed trucks which the city parks for city residents in the evening or weekend will be as provided for in the
fee schedule found in the appendix of this code. (Ordinance 92-12 adopted 9/10/92, Section 9)
Sec. 11.216 Penalty
Any person, firm or corporation violating any of the provisions of this article shall be deemed guilty of a
misdemeanor and upon conviction, shall be subject to a fine in accordance with the general penalty provision
found in Section 1.106 of this code. (Ordinance 93-13 adopted 12/9/93)
ARTICLE 11.300 PUBLIC UTILITIES†
Sec. 11.301 Definitions
(a) Corporation. When used in this article means a private corporation, an association, a joint stock company
or a business trust.
(b) Person. When used in this article means a natural person, a partnership or two or more persons having a
joint or common interest in a corporation as hereinbefore defined.
(c) Public utility or utility. When used in this article includes persons and corporations or their lessees,
trustees, receivers, their agents and servants, now or hereafter owning or operating in the city any wires, poles,
lines, conduit lines, pipes, pipe lines, plant, property or equipment, while using any of the streets or alleys within
the city, for the purpose of carrying on its business or the sale of its commodity or service to the citizens of
Seymour, in either one or more of the following lines:
(1) Producing, manufacturing or obtaining, conveying, distributing or delivering gas, and by “gas”
as used in this article is meant natural gas, artificial gas, mixed gas, either or all for public use, or
service for compensation.
(2) Owning, leasing or operating pipes, pipe lines or any part thereof, manholes or any and all
appliances of whatsoever character in, over or under any street or alley within the city in the
construction, maintaining, operating in the transportation or conveying of sewerage, or in the
operation of any sanitary sewerage disposal plant or any part thereof in the city under franchise or
contract with the city or any person or corporation in the city.
(3) Producing, generating, transmitting, conveying or delivering electricity for the production of
light, heat or power for public use or for the use of any person, firm or corporation within the city for
compensation.
(4) Conveying, carrying or transmitting messages, conversations or communications by telephone
where such service is offered to the public or persons or firms or corporations within the city for
compensation.
(d) The above definitions are cumulative only and not exclusive and any person, including the city, engaged
in any phase of the gas, electric power, electric light or telephone business or sanitary sewerage or any one or
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 136/221
more of such businesses within the city in such manner as to be effected with a public interest, is declared to be
a public utility and subject to all the provisions of this article.
(e) Public utility. Shall, for rate making purposes only, include any person as hereinbefore defined including
the City of Seymour, producing, generating or furnishing any of the foregoing services to another person for
distribution to or for the public for compensation.
(f) Rate. When used in this article means and includes every compensation, charge, fare, toll, rental and
classification or any of them demanded, charged, observed or collected by any public utility for any service,
product or commodity offered by it to the public or to any person, firm or corporation within the city, and rules,
regulations, practices or contracts affecting any such compensation, charge, fee, toll, rental or classification.
Every rate made, demanded or received by any public utility within the city or by two or more public utilities
jointly shall be just and reasonable and every public utility shall furnish adequate, efficient and reasonable
service.
(1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article 1, Section 17-1)
Sec. 11.302 Ability of Council to Gather Information
For the performance of the duties of the city council and the enforcement of this article relative to public utilities,
the council may appoint, employ, or remove such engineers, accountants, statisticians, assistants, inspectors,
clerks, examiners and such subordinates as may from time to time become reasonably necessary to gather
data and information as to the reasonableness of rates to be fixed, charged and collected by any public utility
within the city; and may appoint, on such terms as may be advisable, counsel and attorneys who are specially
skilled in rate matters, and such counsel and attorneys shall advise the council and represent it and the city in
conjunction with the city attorney in all litigation and court proceedings under the direction of the city council,
and the city council shall have the power and authority to have brought before it at any reasonable time any
officer, manager, agent or servant or employer of any public utility doing business in the city and compel them
to testify and give evidence, and submit evidence to the city council at any hearing or investigation before the
city council in any matters involving the fixing of rates or compensation to be charged and collected by such
public utility, and shall have the power and authority to compel any manager, agent or servant or employee of
any public utility to bring before the city council any records, books or accounts of any public utility and submit
the same to the city council for inspection and investigation at any hearing or investigation provided for under
this article, or which at any time may be held within the discretion of the city council. (1988 Seymour City Code,
Chapter 17, Article 1, Section 17-2)
Sec. 11.303 Majority of Council a Quorum
In all matters coming before the city council pertaining to public utilities, a majority of the city council shall
constitute a quorum for the transaction of any business, for the performance of any duty or for the exercise of
any power of the city council. The act of a majority of the city council and all investigations and hearing or
inquiry shall be held by the city council and under its direction and authority. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter
17, Article 1, Section 17-3)
Sec. 11.304 Utilities to File Rate Schedules with City
Within ten (10) days after final passage of this chapter, every public utility within the city or every public utility
doing business in the city shall file with the city secretary schedules showing the rates of compensation being
charged to each of its customers in the city for service or sale of its commodity to each person, firm, partnership
or corporation, and thereafter under such rules and regulations as the city council may from time to time
prescribe, upon demand from the city council, every public utility as herein defined shall file with the city council,
within such time and in such form as the city council may designate, schedules showing the rates being
charged, demanded and collected by such utility for service or sale of its commodity to all persons, firms,
partnerships or corporations in the city. The utility shall keep copies of such schedules open for public
inspection under such rules and regulations as the city council may prescribe. (1988 Seymour City Code,
Chapter 17, Article 1, Section 17-4)
Sec. 11.305 Utilities Not to Give Gifts; Equality of Rates
No public utility doing business within the corporate limits of the city shall directly or indirectly by any device
whatsoever or in any wise, manner or method make any gift or rebate of its service or commodity, nor charge,
demand, collect or receive from any person, firm, partnership or corporation a greater or less compensation for
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 137/221
any service rendered or to be rendered to any of its customers than that as prescribed or as may be prescribed
from time to time by the city council and schedules applicable thereto, nor shall any person receive or accept
any service or any of the utilities commodity the public utility has for sale, for a compensation greater or less
than that prescribed in such schedules or rates as may from time to time be established by the city council;
provided, however, that no public utility shall be prohibited from charging or collecting, whether directly or
indirectly, a greater compensation than that prescribed by ordinance where the city council elects to prescribe
merely minimum rates. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article 1, Section 17-5)
Sec. 11.306 Uniform Rates Required
No public utility shall, as to rate or services, make or grant any unreasonable preference or advantage to any
corporation or person, or subject any corporation or person to any prejudice or disadvantage. No public utility
nor the city council shall establish or maintain any unreasonable difference as to rates or as between classes of
service. The city council shall determine any question of fact arising under this section. (1988 Seymour City
Code, Chapter 17, Article 1, Section 17-6)
Sec. 11.307 Utilities Clothed with Public Interest
Every utility described in this article is hereby declared to be engaged in a business that is affected with a public
interest and is subject to the jurisdiction, control and regulation of the city council in accordance with the
provisions of this article and the laws of Texas. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article 1, Section 17-7)
Sec. 11.308 Public Hearing Authorized in Rate Determination
The city council for the purpose of determining, fixing and regulating the charges, fares, rates or compensation
and/or prescribing maximum and/or minimum rates of any public utility now enjoying or that may hereafter enjoy
any franchise granted by the city, or exercise any other public privilege in the city, or for the purpose of
prescribing the kind of service to be furnished by such utility and the manner in which it shall be rendered and
for the purpose of from time to time altering or changing such rules, regulations and compensation, shall at the
request of the public utility affected, or upon call of the chairman of the council or call of a majority of the
council, either at a regular meeting of the council or a special meeting called for that purpose, have a hearing
before the council. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article 1, Section 17-8)
Sec. 11.309 Notice of Hearing Required
The city council shall cause at least ten (10) days prior notice, by registered mail, to be given to any public
utility, person, firm or corporation affected by such hearing. Such notice shall state the time and place of such
meeting the purpose thereof. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article 1, Section 17-9)
Sec. 11.310 Utilities' Records Available to City
In order to ascertain all the facts necessary for a proper understanding of what is or could be a reasonable rate
or compensation, the public utility shall on demand submit to the city council or any person designated by it for
inspection, its books, records and schedules of rates charged, as well as the rates proposed to be charged, and
the city council shall have full power to compel the attendance of witnesses for such purpose before any
hearing before the council. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article 1, Section 17-10).
Sec. 11.311 Fair and Reasonable Rates to be Set by Ordinance
The city council after such hearing and notice shall by ordinance from time to time determine and fix such rates
and/or prescribe such maximum and/or minimum rates and enforce such schedules of rates to be charged and
collected by such public utility for its services or commodity furnished to its patrons or to any persons, firms,
partnerships or corporations in the city. Such rates so established or fixed shall be just, fair and reasonable
rates or charges for the services or commodities furnished by the public utility, and all regulations for
transmitting, carrying, conveying, producing, transporting, distributing, selling and delivering such commodities
within the city shall be fair and reasonable. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article 1, Section 17-11)
Sec. 11.312 City Council May Amend Rates
Any utility affected by a schedule of rates fixed by the city council or any regulations thereof, or any person, firm
or corporation thus affected, may by petition, or the city council on its own motion, after notice and hearing, may
change, alter or modify any existing rate or rates or regulations and amend or substitute an entirely new rate
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 138/221
structure and make such further schedule of rates and/or regulations by ordinance, resolution or orders as may
be consistent with fair and reasonable rates to be charged patrons of such public utility within the corporate
limits of the city for the commodity furnished or service rendered. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article
1, Section 17-12)
Sec. 11.313 Right of Appeal
The council assumes original regulatory jurisdiction in the regulations, compensations, fixing and regulating the
charges, fares or rates of any public utility, person, firm or corporation now enjoying, or that may hereafter
enjoy, the privilege of any franchise or exercising any other public privilege as hereinbefore set forth in this
article, and any public utility, person, firm or corporation who shall desire to contest any rate schedule or rates
or compensation or regulations as may from time to time be fixed by the city council, shall have the right to
appeal therefrom to any agency or court of competent jurisdiction. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17,
Article 1, Section 17-13)
Sec. 11.314 Discrimination by Utility Prohibited
No utility shall unreasonably discriminate in favor against any person, place or corporation either in apportioning
the supply of its commodities or its charges therefor. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article 1, Section
17-14)
Sec. 11.315 City Council May Set Standards
The city council may, after hearing and notice, as hereinbefore provided for, upon its own motion or complaint,
ascertain and fix just and reasonable standards, classifications, regulations, practices or services to be
furnished, imposed, observed and followed by any utility; ascertain and fix adequate and reasonable standards
for the measurements of quantity, quality, pressure, initial voltage or other conditions pertaining to the supply of
the product, commodity or service furnished or rendered by any utility; prescribe reasonable regulations for the
examination and testing of such products, commodity or service and for the measurement thereof; establish
and approve reasonable rules, regulations, specifications and standards to secure the accuracy of all meters
and appliances for the measurement; and provide for the examination and testing of any and all appliances
used for the measurement of product, commodity or service of any utility. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter
17, Article 1, Section 17-15)
Sec. 11.316 City May Fix Value of Utility Property
The city council may, on hearing and notice, ascertain and fix the value of the whole or any part of the property
of any utility, insofar as the same us material to the exercise of the jurisdiction of the city council and may make
revaluation from time to time and ascertains the value of all new construction, extension and additions to the
property of every utility. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article 1, Section 17-16)
Sec. 11.317 Utility Accounting System
Each utility shall establish a system of accounts to be kept as may be ordered and directed by the city council
or establish a system of accounts for each class and the city council may prescribe the manner in which its boor
accounts in some particular form or manner, such practice may be continued and compliance with such
regulations be deemed compliance with the regulations of the city council. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter
17, Article 1, Section 17-17)
Sec. 11.318 City Authorized to Examine, Test Utilities
Any utility shall permit the city council and officers and employees of the city during all reasonable hours to
enter upon any premises occupied by any utility for the purpose of making the examination and tests and
exercising any power provided for in this article, and shall permit the setting up and use on such premises of
any apparatus and appliance necessary therefor. Such utility shall have the right to be represented at the
making of such examination, test, and inspection. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article 1, Section 17-
18)
Sec. 11.319 Utility Reports to Council
Each utility shall file with the city council annual reports in such form and of such content as the city council may
require, and special reports concerning any matters about which the city council is authorized to inquire or keep
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 139/221
itself informed, and which it is required under this article to enforce. All reports shall be made under oath when
required by the city council. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article 1, Section 17-19)
Sec. 11.320 City May Investigate Utility Management
The city council may on its own motion and whenever it may deem necessary in the performance of its duties
investigate and examine the conditions and management of any utility. In conducting such investigation, the city
council may proceed, either with or without a hearing as it may deem best, but it shall make no order without
the parties thereto a hearing. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article 1, Section 17-20)
Sec. 11.321 Authority to Issue Subpoena
In all hearings before the city council or investigations by the city council it may issue subpoena duces tecum
and all necessary process in proceedings pending before it; which may be served by the city council or by any
person authorized to serve process of courts of record. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article 1,
Section 17-21)
Sec. 11.322 Depositions
The city council or any party to the proceedings may in any investigation or hearing before the city council
cause the depositions of witnesses to be taken in the manner prescribed by law for the taking of depositions in
civil cases. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article 1, Section 17-22)
Sec. 11.323 Adherence to Law Required
Any public utility coming under the provisions of this article, or any manager, agent or servant or employee of
any public utility failing or refusing to subject itself or himself to the jurisdiction of the city council as provided for
in this article and failing or refusing to obey any order or ordinance of the city council legally promulgated
hereunder, after reasonable notice and opportunity to do so, shall be liable to a penalty as hereinafter provided.
(1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article 1, Section 17-23)
Sec. 11.324 Construing Penalty Provision
In construing and enforcing the provisions of this article relating to penalties, the act, omission or failure of any
official, agent or employee of any corporation or person acting within the scope of his official duties or
employment, shall in every case be deemed to be also the act, omission or failure of such corporation or
person. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article 1, Section 17-24)
Sec. 11.325 Penalties Cumulative
All penalties accruing under this article shall be cumulative and a suit may be brought by the city in any court
having jurisdiction thereof against any utility for the recovery of such penalties, and a suit for the recovery of
one penalty shall not be a bar to or affect the recovery of any penalty for forfeiture or be a bar to any criminal
prosecution against any public utility or any official, director, agent or employee thereof or any other corporation
or person. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article 1, Section 17-25)
Sec. 11.326 Actions to Recover Penalties
Actions to recover penalties under this article shall be brought in the name of the City of Seymour, and all
criminal prosecutions shall be brought in the name of the State of Texas. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter
17, Article 1, Section 17-26)
Sec. 11.327 City Not Exempt from Provisions
Nothing in this article shall in any manner be construed as exempting the city, which owns and operates a
public utility, from any of the provisions or operation of this or any other ordinance hereafter passed relative to
any of the subject matters contained in this article. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article 1, Section 17-
27)
ARTICLE 11.400 WATER, SEWER, AND ELECTRIC SYSTEMS*
Sec. 11.401 Certain Acts Unlawful
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 140/221
It shall be unlawful for any person or persons to do, commit, or assist in committing any of the following things
or acts in the city:
(1) To open or close any fire hydrant or stopcock connected with the waterworks system of the
city, or lift or remove the covers of any gate valves or shut-offs thereof, without the permission of the
city waterworks representative, except in case of fire, and then under the direction of officers of the
fire department.
(2) To interfere with, destroy, deface, impair, injure or wantonly force open any gate or door, or in
any way whatsoever destroy, injure or deface any part of any engine house, reservoir, stand pipe,
elevated tank, building or buildings, or appurtenances, fences, trees, shrubs, or fixtures or property
appertaining to the waterworks system, wastewater treatment plant and sanitary sewer system.
(3) To place any telegraph, telephone, electric light pole, or any obstruction whatsoever within
three (3) feet of any fire hydrant.
(4) To go upon or ascend the stairway or steps on any elevated water storage tank or stand pipe
of the waterworks system, except by permission of the waterworks representative.
(5) To resort to any fraudulent device or arrangement for the purpose of procuring water for
himself or others from private connections on premises contrary to city regulations or ordinances.
(6) To interfere with or injure any reservoir, tank, fountain, hydrant, pipe, cock, valve, or other
apparatus pertaining to the waterworks system, or to turn on or off without authority the water in any
street hydrant or other water fixture, or to hitch or tie any animal thereto.
(7) To make or permit to be made any connections with the main or service pipes of the
waterworks system or to turn on or use the water of said system without first obtaining a permit
therefor.
(8) To cover over or conceal from view any water valve box, service or meter box.
(9) To remove any water meter that has been placed by the city, or in any manner change,
interfere with or tamper with any water meter; providing the provisions of this section shall not apply
to the employees of the city when acting in their official capacities.
(10) To turn on the water supply to any building or to any supply pipe where the supply has been
turned off for the non-payment of the monthly water charge or for the violation of any rule or
ordinance governing the waterworks system.
(1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article 2, Section 17-31)
Sec. 11.402 Relocation of Existing Water Meters, Waterlines, Etc.
In instances where existing water meters, waterlines and other related waterworks items are requested to be
relocated, by a person, firm, association or corporation, for the convenience of said person, firm, association or
corporation, the actual expenses for the relocation shall be borne solely by the person, firm, association or
corporation requesting the relocation. The actual work can be performed by city forces or by a contractor
selected by the city. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article 2, Section 17-32)
Sec. 11.403 Variance
In instances where the relocation of existing water meters, waterlines and other related waterworks are
requested by a person, firm, association or corporation as heretofore mentioned in Section 11.402, and in a
determination by the city administrator that said relocation shall benefit the city, the city administrator shall then
prorate the actual costs between the party requesting the relocation and the city. (1988 Seymour City Code,
Chapter 17, Article 2, Section 17-33)
Sec. 11.404 Electric Deposit
Persons, firms and corporations desiring electric service to be furnished by the city shall make deposits prior to
such connections being made, which deposits shall be made and paid to the city in amounts as provided for in
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 141/221
the fee schedule found in the appendix of this code. (Ordinance 95-5, adopted 11/17/95, Section 1)
Sec. 11.405 Water Deposit
Those desiring water service from the city shall deposit prior to receiving any such water service connection
and with the city in amounts as provided for in the fee schedule found in the appendix of this code. (Ordinance
95-5, adopted 11/16/95, Section 2)
Sec. 11.405.1 Garbage-Only Deposit
Person living outside the city limits, having no other utilities with the city but desiring to be served by the city's
solid waste collection contractor, shall deposit, prior to receiving a solid waste receptacle, a garbage-only
deposit with the utility billing department in the amount provided in Appendix A to this code.
Sec. 11.405.2 Refund of Garbage-Only Deposit
(a) The garbage-only deposit may be refunded in whole or in part if account holder presents to city hall or
otherwise provides signature and dated request in writing for termination of garbage-only service and the
removal of trash receptacle.
(b) When said account is paid in full and request for service terminated is received before the 6th of the
calendar month (or date when bills are printed for that month) customer may receive a full refund. Partial
refunds will be granted of deposit less the amount of final bill if termination request is received after monthly
bills are drafted. If trash receptacle is damaged or lost, the accountholder forfeits his/her refund. For special
circumstances refunds will be made at city administrator's or city secretary's discretion.
(Ordinance 2006-02 adopted 3/23/06)
Sec. 11.406 Additional Deposit, Unpaid Balances
If the city determines, by a search of the records of the city, that any customer applying for service has had
previous unpaid balances for city electric or water service, it may, at its discretion, cause said customer to make
an additional deposit to the city. (Ordinance 95-5, adopted 11/16/95, Section 3)
Sec. 11.407 Waiver of Deposit
If the customer applying for service can present to the city a valid letter of credit from one or more previous
electric and/or water suppliers for a period of not less than one year, the city can, at its discretion, waive all or
part of any required electric and/or water deposits prescribed in Sections 11.404, 11.405, and 11.406 above.
(Ordinance 95-5, adopted 11/16/95, Section 4)
Sec. 11.408 Identification Required
The city shall require, or cause to be required, positive and personal identification of any or all persons applying
for electric or water service from the city prior to any connection of said service. (Ordinance 95-5, adopted
11/16/95, Section 5)
Sec. 11.409 Disconnection for Default; Reconnection Charge*
In the event any consumer of electricity or water within the city, and using such city facilities does not pay the
matured rates and charges within fifteen (15) days from the day that same becomes due and payable, then the
city shall cause such electrical, or water service so in default to be disconnected. In the event of any such
disconnection for failure to pay accounts as stated, the customer shall pay to the city a reconnection charge,
before reconnection is made, in the amount as provided for in the fee schedule found in the appendix of this
code, plus the full account and charges that are unpaid at that time; and upon such payments being made,
such connection shall be reestablished. If it is determined that any disconnected water or electric meter has
been illegally turned on or tampered with in any manner by anyone other than a city employee, the meter will be
removed and reinstalled only upon payment of additional service charge as provided for in the fee schedule
