found in the appendix of this code. (Ordinance 95-5, adopted 11/16/95, Section 6)
Sec. 11.410 Reserved†
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 142/221
Sec. 11.411 No Free Service Allowed
No free service shall be allowed; and to the extent that the city or any of its agents or instrumentalities may
avail themselves of the services and facilities afforded by the system, they shall pay therefor the same rates
and charges herein prescribed. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article 2, Section 17-48)
Sec. 11.412 Refund of Deposits Under $1.01
Whenever the light or water deposit, after liquidation charges, is less than one dollar and one cent ($1.01) the
person involved shall pick that amount up at the utility office in person. If said amount is not picked up within
ninety (90) calendar days after notification, said amount shall revert to the utility company. (1988 Seymour City
Code, Chapter 17, Article 2, Section 17-49)
Sec. 11.413 Water Rates; Service Fee; Capital Improvements
(a) The rates for water furnished by the city to residents inside the city limits shall be as provided for in the
fee schedule found in the appendix of this code.
(b) The minimum rates for water furnished by the city to customers outside the city limits shall be as provided
for in the fee schedule found in the appendix of this code.
(c) A service fee as provided for in the fee schedule found in the appendix of this code shall be assessed for
customer-requested connects and disconnects, other than those required to initiate or terminate service to a
location, during regular office hours Monday through Friday, 8:00 a.m. to 5:00 p.m., and a service fee as
provided for in the fee schedule found in the appendix of this code for customer-requested connects and
disconnects, after office hours. Said fee to be charged for both disconnect/connect as a single service, to be
attached to and made part of the next regular billing.
(d) A Water Capital Improvements Fund is hereby established from a portion of the revenues created by this
section, to be funded as provided for in the fee schedule found in the appendix of this code. Said Capital
Improvement Fund to be separately maintained at the sole discretion of the city council for use in Water Capital
Improvements projects only.
(e) The city council expressly reserves the privilege of negotiating contracts for utility abatements for
commercial customers and entities who are by their nature, in the opinion of the council, necessities or
enhancements for this community. The council, therefore, reserves the right to waive or abate customary
charges for utilities as the council deem appropriate.
(1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article 2, Section 17-50; Ordinance 96-12, adopted 11/21/96, Section 3)
Sec. 11.414 Water Supply to Airport; Charges
The City of Seymour shall install a two (2) inch water line adjacent to the lots leased to the lessees at the
Seymour Municipal Airport. Service lines, three-quarter (3/4) inch in diameter, will be provided to each lot or
hangar with an outlet. The cost of the water service line, water tap, and monthly service shall be as provided for
in the fee schedule found in the appendix of this code. (Ordinance 89-6 adopted 8/3/89)
Sec. 11.415 Discontinuance of Service; Unpaid Balance
In the event the monthly service charge is not paid, service will be discontinued and the unpaid balance will be
assessed against the lessee's annual lease agreements. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article 2,
Section 17-52)
Sec. 11.416 Private Water Line Restrictions
Lessees at the Seymour Municipal Airport desiring to install water lines not connecting to the city's main water
line shall require authorization from the city administrator. Any private water line installed shall be maintained by
the lessee utilizing said water line. Any liability incurred through the installation or use of said water line shall be
borne entirely be the lessee. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article 2, Section 17-53)
Sec. 11.417 Cost of Water Meters, Installation in Plainview Addition
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 143/221
There is hereby set an average current cost for water meters and water meter installation for existing water
meter taps in the Plainview Addition to the city. The average current cost of the water meter and water meter
installation materials shall be determined by the current cost of said materials at the time of installation. The
cost shall be payable in advance before a water meter is set. The cost shall apply only to new construction after
December 8, 1977. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article 2, Section 17-54)
Sec. 11.418 Reserved*
Sec. 11.419 Connection to Sewer System Required
Before any building permit is issued to any person or persons, firm or corporation, to erect a building, any public
house or residence within the corporate limits of the city, and within one hundred fifty (150) feet of the line of the
sewer system of the city, such person or persons, firm or corporation shall show to the building inspector that
the plans for such building and improvements provide for a proper connection with the sanitary sewer line.
(1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article 2, Section 17-57)
Sec. 11. 420 Privies Prohibited
Any person, persons, firm or corporation who shall improve any property within one hundred fifty (150) feet of
the sewer line, and include it in such improvements, and who shall erect or maintain any privy or dry closet,
permitting the same to be used, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor, and such act is hereby prohibited. (1988
Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article 2, Section 17-58)
Sec. 11. 421 Miscellaneous Service Charges
(a) Temporary Service and/or Changing of Service Entrance. Temporary service is service through a “service
entrance” that is temporarily installed. This “temporary service” may be for a new residence while under
construction or it may be during repair of an old residence or for any other service of a temporary nature. This
would include changing a “house service” to a “meter pole service” or to change from a “meter pole” to the
“house”. This “temporary service” will also apply to non-residential service. The fee for this service shall be as
provided for in the fee schedule found in the appendix of this code.
(b) Location Change Fee. If a customer moves from one location to another and the city disconnects and
reconnects his water and electric meters, the fee for this service will be as provided for in the fee schedule
found in the appendix of this code.
(c) Re-Read at Customer's Request. Meters will be re-read by customer request. There will be a fee as
provided for in the fee schedule found in the appendix of this code, if the original reading was correct. There will
be no charge for an incorrect reading, and an adjustment of billing will be made to correct an error in reading.
(d) Connect Fee. A service charge for connecting utility service (turning utilities on and reading meters) shall
be as provided for in the fee schedule found in the appendix of this code.
(e) Recourse for Non-Payment of Service Charges. Statements will be issued for the service charges herein
contained, to be mailed by the first of each month following service. Any service charges remaining unpaid
thirty days after billing date will be added to utility bills as “arrears”, and failure to pay total bill as stated on utility
statement will result in disconnection of utility services.
(Ordinance 95-5, adopted 11/16/95, Section 8)
Sec. 11.422 Electric Utility Rates
(a) Charges for customers purchasing electrical energy and obtaining electrical services from the city shall be
as prescribed from time to time by the city council.
(b) Referencing all rates, a Correction Factor to adjust prior months estimated KWH sales to actual and
reflect over and under recoveries of purchased power costs, is hereby added to the Power Cost Adjustment
Factor (PCAF) that is attached as Exhibit I.
(1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article 2, Section 17-60)
ARTICLE 11.500 NATURAL GAS
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 144/221
Sec. 11.501 Standard Gas Code Adopted
The Standard Gas Code, 1985 edition with 1986 revisions, is hereby adopted by reference as though fully
copied herein. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article 3, Section 17-71)
Sec. 11.502 Gas Rates
The maximum general service rate for sales of natural gas rendered to residential and commercial consumers
within the city limits of Seymour, Texas, by Lone Star Gas Company, a Division of ENSERCH CORPORATION,
a Texas Corporation, its successors and assigns, is hereby fixed and determined as set forth in Item A, in the
Attachment hereto which is incorporated herein. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article 3, Section 17-
72)
Sec. 11.503 Adjustments
(a) The residential and commercial rates set forth above shall be adjusted upward or downward from a base
of ($4.3142) per Mcf by a Gas Cost Adjustment Factor expressed as an amount per thousand cubic feet (Mcf)
of natural gas for changes in the intracompany city gate rate charge as authorized by the Railroad Commission
of Texas or other regulatory body having jurisdiction for gas delivered to the Seymour distribution system,
according to Item B, in the Attachment hereto which is incorporated herein.
(b) Company shall also receive tax adjustments according to Item C, in the Attachment hereto which is
incorporated herein.
(1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article 3, Section 17-73)
Sec. 11.504 Service Charges
In addition to the aforesaid rates, Company shall have the right to collect such reasonable charges as are
necessary to conduct its business and to carry out its reasonable rules and regulations in effect. The service
charges set forth in Item D and E, in the Attachment hereto which is incorporated herein are approved. Services
for which no charge is set out may be performed and charged for by Company at a level established by the
normal forces of competition. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article 3, Section 17-74)
Sec. 11.505 Rate Case Expenses
Rate case expense is not included in the calculation of proposed rates. If rate case expense is incurred in this
current case, it is the intention of Lone Star Gas Company to recover the current and any prior rate case
expense through a surcharge designed for a six-month nominal recovery period. The surcharge per Mcf would
be calculated by dividing the rate case expense to be recovered by one-half of the adjusted annual sales
volume to residential and commercial customers. When a surcharge is applicable, monthly status reports will be
provided to account for the collections. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 17, Article 3, Section 17-75)
Sec. 11.506 Amendments, Changes to Rates
The rates set forth in this article may be changed and amended by either the city or Company in the manner
provided by law. Service hereunder is subject to the orders of regulatory bodies having jurisdiction, and to the
Company's Rules and Regulations currently on file in the Company's office. (1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter
17, Article 3, Section 17-76)
ARTICLE 11.600 CONNECTIONS, REPAIRS AND EXTENSIONS OF WATER AND SEWER SERVICE
Sec. 11.601 Connections, Repairs and Extensions of Water Service
(a) The city shall install and maintain all service connections and lines from water mains to the customer's
meter (limit 100') and it shall be unlawful for any plumber or other person to repair or renew a service line from
the main to the meter.
(b) It shall be unlawful for any plumber or other person other than City Water Department personnel to tap
any water main, make connection with the water main or extend a service line from the main. Said work shall
be done exclusively by the City Water Department personnel and the customer shall pay the customary tapping
fee.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 145/221
(c) The city will extend new service lines one hundred (100) feet or to the nearest property line. New service
line extensions shall be done exclusively by the City Water Department personnel.
(d) Any extensions beyond one hundred (100) feet shall be installed by the city but paid for by the customer
and the city will then maintain the lines.
(Ordinance 93-2, adopted 2/18/93, Section 1)
Sec. 11.602 Connections, Repairs and Extensions of Sewer Service
(a) The City Sewer Department personnel shall make all taps to sewer mains and install risers to the correct
height required for the customer's service line and shall maintain the same. The customer will be required to
pay the customary tapping fee. It shall be the customer's responsibility to install, repair and maintain his sewer
line fro- the riser to his house or building.
(b) It shall be unlawful for any plumber or other person other than City Sewer Department personnel to tap
any sewer main or install risers.
(c) The city will extend new main lines one hundred (100) feet or to the nearest property line. New main line
extensions shall be done exclusively by the City Water Department personnel.
(d) Any extensions beyond one hundred (100) feet shall be installed by the city but paid for by the customer
and the city will then maintain the lines. These extensions shall be 6" or larger and the customer shall pay for a
4" line.
(e) In the event a lift station is required for a property owner to connect to city sewer service the property
owner will pay for the lift station and equipment and the city will assume maintenance of the station once it is
installed. The lift station must be built to city specifications and inspected by the city prior to the city accepting
maintenance responsibilities for the station. The customer will pay for electrical service to operate the lift
station.
(Ordinance 93-2, adopted 2/18/93, Section 2)
ARTICLE 11.700 ELECTRICAL UTILITIES BOARD
Sec. 11.701 Board Created; Composition; Organization; Qualifications
(a) There is hereby created an Electric Utilities Board.
(b) The city council will appoint three (3) members to the Electrical Utilities Board. The city administrator,
Electrical Superintendent, and Electrical Trainee shall be ex-officio members of the Board. They shall attend
meetings of the Board and shall have the right to discuss any matter that is under consideration by the board
but shall have no vote. They shall provide all information requested by the Board in a timely manner.
(c) At the first organizational meeting, the appointed members will draw for terms as follows: One (1) shall
draw a one-year term, and one (1) shall draw a two year term, and one (1) shall draw a three (3) year term. A
member successor shall be appointed for a three (3) year term. Vacancies shall be filled for any unexpired term
in the same manner, as provided for regular appointments.
(d) Members of the Electrical Utilities Board shall have the same qualifications as are required for
membership on the city council.
(1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 5, Article 4, Section 5-101)
Sec. 11.702 Board's Duties
(a) The board shall serve the city council as a consulting and advisory body to study and recommend policies
relating to the operation and future planning of the electric department.
(b) The annual budget for the department shall be prepared by the electric superintendent and the city
administrator. The board shall review the budget and make such changes as they deem appropriate. The city
administrator shall then present it to the Council, with the general budget, for their review.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 146/221
(c) The board shall make all recommendations for capital improvements to the city council.
(1988 Seymour City Code, Chapter 5, Article 4, Section 5-102)
ARTICLE 11.800 ELECTRICITY RULES, REGULATIONS AND RATES*
Sec. 11.801 Definitions
Company, Utility or Public Utility. All persons, firms, or corporations, private or municipal, now or hereafter
operating in the city, any generating plants and distribution systems, any wires, poles, or lines, property or
equipment, while using any of the streets or alleys within said city, for the purpose of carrying on its business or
generating, distributing, or selling electric power and current for any purpose.
Consumer or Customer. A person, firm or corporation using any electric power from any company, as herein
above defined.
Net Rate. The rate as set out in said schedules herein.
Sec. 11.802 Schedules
The schedules or rates as provided for in the fee schedule found in appendix A of this code are hereby adopted
and fixed as the minimum rates which may and or shall be charged for electric service hereinafter furnished to
any consumer or customer, as above defined.
Sec. 11.803 Power Cost Adjustment Factor
The monthly charges for all rates shall be adjusted in accordance to the power cost adjustment factor (PCAF)
that is attached as exhibit A to Ordinance 2014-02.
Sec. 11.804 Policy Statement
Referencing fees, service, location or installation of facilities, rules and regulations, etc., that is hereby attached,
as exhibit B to Ordinance 2014-02, a policy statement.
Sec. 11.805 Rules and Regulations
(a) The utility will require reasonable security for the payment of its bills, and shall not furnish service to any
customer who is in default in payment of any indebtedness for electric current to the utility. The following
procedures are established to ensure the security of payment:
(1) Residential electric customers deposit will be as provided in the fee schedule found in
appendix A of this code, providing that customer does not owe a past due bill, otherwise, it will be at
the discretion of the city administrator or city secretary on how much the deposit will be.
(2) A valid current (within the previous 12 months) letter of credit from one or more previous
electric suppliers, of not less than one year, showing an excellent record of payment.
(3) Commercial electric customers deposit will equal to a two-month average bill. In the event of
new construction where no monthly average bill exists, the deposit will be computed from a previous
bill similar to location. The deposit will never be less than as provided in the fee schedule found in
appendix A of this code.
(4) A valid current (within the previous 12 months) letter of credit from one or more previous
electric suppliers, of not less than one year showing an excellent record of payment [sic].
(5) If the city determines, by a search of the records of the city, that any customer applying for
service has had previous unpaid balances for city utility service, said customer will be required to
pay unpaid balances in full, plus deposits before service can be established with the city. This
applies to both commercial and residential.
(6) The city shall require, or cause to be required, positive and personal identification of any or all
persons applying for electric service from the city, prior to any connection of said service.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 147/221
(7) In the event any consumer of electricity within the city, and using such city facilities does not
pay utility charges by the 18th or the first business day thereafter, then the city shall cause such
electrical services in default to be disconnected. In the event of any such disconnection for failure to
pay accounts as stated, the customer shall pay to the city, a reconnection fee charge, before the
reconnection is made, in the sum provided in the fee schedule found in appendix A of this code.
Reconnection will be made, (if payment is received in the city office no later than 5:00 p.m.,
Monday–Friday, excluding holidays) and upon such payment being made, such connection shall be
reestablished. If it is determined that any disconnected electric meter has been illegally turned on or
tampered with in any manner by anyone other than a city employee, the meter will be removed and
reinstalled, only upon payment of an additional service charge as provided in the fee schedule found
in appendix A of this code. A fine of up to $500.00 will be imposed and charges will also be filed in
municipal court, under theft of service charge. If court payment is not received as court ordered,
electric service will be subject to disconnection until payment of utility service and court cost is
received in full.
(Ordinance 2014-02 adopted 3/20/14)
(8) Refund (applying to both residential and commercial accounts) of utility deposits, will be
applied to the customers utility bill, if in the previous 18 months from the date deposits were paid, all
payments have been promptly paid (no exceptions). (Ordinance 2018-12 adopted 11/15/18)
(9) The charge for return checks or drafts will be provided in the fee schedule found in appendix A
of this code. After 3 occurrences, you will no longer be able to pay by check or draft, for a period of
one year.
(b) Bills will be rendered by the utility office on the 7th day of each month, and shall be paid by the consumer
to the city the 18th day of each month, and shall become due and payable on this date. Any customer paying
after the 18th day of the month, will be charged a 10% penalty on their remaining balance.
(c) Late notices will be sent out on the 19th of the month, with payment due in full by the 25th. If payment is
not received by the 26th at 10:00 a.m., services will be disconnected without further notice.
(d) Electric service will not be turned off for failure of payment on Fridays or any day prior to holidays. Also,
on days of extreme conditions, those conditions being temperature forecasting above 100 degrees (F) for 3 or
more days and temperature forecasted below 32 degrees (F) for a 24-hour period.
(e) Average monthly billing for residential customers by executing an average monthly payment (AMP)
agreement.
(f) Wiring, apparatus, machinery or appliances of the consumer will be required to be installed and
maintained in accordance with good electric practices, all governmental regulations and wiring permit is
required.
(g) The ordinary method of connection between the utility's distributing system and the consumer's service
wires will be by overhead wires. If the consumer shall desire to have connection made in any way, special
arrangements will be made between the consumer and the utility by which the connection will be made and
maintained at the consumer's cost.
(h) The utility will, without rental or other charge, furnish a meter for the registration of electric current. The
city has the right to inspect such meter at any time and to pass such regulations as to testing it as may be
necessary to ascertain and ensure its accuracy and efficiency.
(i) The consumer shall provide and at all times maintain, free of expense to the utility, and at a suitable and
easily accessible location within the premises to be supplied with electric current, sufficient and proper space
for the installation of meters or other similar devices of the utility, and shall also provide the necessary meter
board, wiring, and meter loops.
(j) The utility will supply electric current only through meters or other measuring devices furnished and owned
by it. The utility office must be notified when the consumer desires to have such meter or other measuring
device installed, relocated, changed or removed.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 148/221
(k) The duly authorized agents of the utility shall have access at all reasonable hours to the premises of the
consumer for the purpose of inspecting wiring and apparatus, removing the utility's property, reading meters
and other purposes incident to the carrying out of the contract. The utility, however, does not assume the duty
of inspecting the consumer's wiring, machinery or apparatus, and will not be responsible therefor.
(l) The consumer shall properly protect the utility's property on the consumer's premises, and shall permit no
one but the utility's agents, and persons authorized by law, to inspect or tamper with the utility's wiring and
apparatus.
(m) The consumer assumes all responsibility for the electric current upon the consumer's premises, and at
and from the point of delivery thereof, and for the wires, apparatus and appurtenances used in connection
therewith.
Sec. 11.806 Miscellaneous Service Charges
(a) Temporary Service and/or Changing of Service Entrance. Temporary service is service through a “service
entrance” that is temporarily installed. This “temporary service” may be during repair of an old residence or for
any other service of a temporary nature. This would include changing a “house service” to a “meter pole
service” or to change from a “meter pole” to the “house.” This “temporary service” will also apply to
nonresidential service. The fee for this service shall be provided in the fee schedule found in appendix A of this
code.
(b) Location Change Fee. If a customer moves from one location to another and the city disconnects and
reconnects the electric meter, the fee for this service will be provided in the fee schedule found in appendix A of
this code.
(c) Reread at Customer's Request. Meters will be reread by customer request. There will be a fee charged
provided in the fee schedule found in appendix A of this code, if the original reading was correct. There will be
no charge for an incorrect reading, and an adjustment of billing will be made to correct an error in reading.
(d) Connect Fee (Establishing Services). A service charge for connecting utility service (turning utilities on
and reading meters) shall be a charge provided in the fee schedule found in appendix A of this code during
regular office hours.
(e) Recourse for Nonpayment of Service Charges. Statements will be issued for the service charges herein
contained, to be mailed by the 7th of each month following service. Any service charges remaining unpaid thirty
days after billing date will be added to utility bills as “arrears,” and failure to pay total bill as stated on utility
statement will result in disconnection of utility services.
Sec. 11.807 Penalties
(a) Any person, firm or corporation as defined herein in section 11.801 above who violates any provision of
this article or who fails, omits, or neglects to obey or comply with any lawful order or ordinance or any part of
this provision thereof, legally promulgated by the city council, involving any of the matters herein contained
upon conviction in a court of competent jurisdiction, shall be fined any sum of money not to exceed $500.00 for
each offense; and each day of such violation, omission or neglect to obey or comply with such order or
ordinances promulgated hereunder shall be deemed a separate offense.
(b) In construing and enforcing the provisions of this article relating to penalties, the act, omission or failure of
any official, agent, servant or employee of any corporation or person acting within the scope of his official duties
or employment shall in every case be deemed to be also the act, omission or failure of such corporation or
person as herein defined.
Sec. 11.808 Free Service
No free service shall be allowed; and to the extent that the city or any of its agencies or instrumentalities may
avail themselves of the services and facilities afforded by the system, they shall pay therefor, the same rates
and charges herein prescribed.
Sec. 11.809 Negotiated Contracts
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 149/221
The city council expressly reserves the right to negotiate contracts for utility abatements, unless contraindicated
by bond ordinance, with commercial customers and entities that are by their nature, in the opinion of the
council, necessities or enhancements for community development. The council, therefore, reserves the right to
waive, abate, or reduce customary charges for utilities as the council deems appropriate.
(Ordinance 2014-02 adopted 3/20/14)
ARTICLE 11.900 GREASE/GRIT TRAPS
Sec. 11.901 Grease/Grit Trap Maintenance
The owner or lessee of every commercial establishment within the city that generates grease or grit trap wastes
shall install and maintain grease/grit traps or control grease/grit wastes in such a manner as will negate the
possibility of flow of said wastes into the city collection system. The grease grit traps shall be cleaned frequently
no less than every six (6) months. Records will be kept by the proprietors of the commercial establishment and
will be made available for inspection by city personnel during normal business hours. New commercial
establishments that generate grease or grit shall install grease/grit traps before opening for business.
Sec. 11.902 Grease/Grit Trap Inspection
All grease/grit traps will be inspected periodically by city personnel. The city shall inspect the facilities of any
user to ascertain whether the purpose of this article is being met and all requirements are being complied with.
Persons or occupants of premises where wastewater is created or discharged shall allow the city, or the
designated representatives of the city, ready access at all reasonable times to all parts of the premises for the
purpose of inspection, sampling, records examination or in the performance of their duties.
(Ordinance 2003-11 adopted 6/19/03)
Sec. 11.903 Disposal
The city will temporarily provide a place for permitted haulers to dispose of grease/grit trap wastes at a rate
charged to the hauler established in section 11.912. (Ordinance 94-1 adopted 3/10/94, Section 3)
Sec. 11.904 Discontinuing Grease/Grit Trap Disposal Service
The city reserves the right to reject any hauled waste consisting of grease/grit trap waste at the city wastewater
facility when such discharges may compromise the effectiveness of the wastewater treatment plant process.
(Ordinance 94-1 adopted 3/10/94, Section 4)
Sec. 11.905 Permitting of Haulers
Grease/grit trap waste haulers disposing of waste at the Seymour Wastewater Treatment Plant will be permitted
by the city to haul said waste. A fee will be charged for this permit at a rate established in Section 11.912. All
haulers will also be required to obtain a permit to haul said wastes from the State and comply with all applicable
State requirements. (Ordinance 94-1 adopted 3/10/94, Section 5)
Sec. 11.906 Accepting Wastes from Outside the City Limits
Grease or grit trap wastes derived from outside of the city limits will not be accepted. (Ordinance 94-1 adopted
3/10/94, Section 6)
Sec. 11.907 Trip Tickets
All hauled waste loads being discharged at the City of Seymour Wastewater Treatment Plant will be
documented on trip tickets that will be supplied by the city at a rate established in Section 11.912. (Ordinance
94-1 adopted 3/10/94, Section 7)
Sec. 11.908 Operation Hours
Wastes can be discharged when allowed at the Wastewater Treatment Plant, between the hours of 10:00 a.m. -
4:00 p.m., Monday through Friday, the plant will be closed on Saturday, Sunday and Holidays. Prior notice of
discharge must be given to the Wastewater Treatment Plant operator on duty. Special requests by haulers
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 150/221
wanting to discharge during non-operating hours, if allowed, will be charged for any overtime incurred by the
operator on duty. (Ordinance 94-1 adopted 3/10/94, Section 8)
Sec. 11.909 Testing of Wastes
All grit traps will be tested by city personnel prior to being loaded by the waste hauler. Notice should be given to
the Wastewater Treatment operator twenty-four (24) hours in advance. Any waste trucks carrying hauled
wastes are subject to testing at any time at the haulers expense and shall be done at the discretion of city
personnel. (Ordinance 94-1 adopted 3/10/94, Section 9)
Sec. 11.910 Rejection of Loads
Any waste deemed to be unacceptable by city personnel will not be allowed to be discharges into the
wastewater treatment facility. (Ordinance 94-1 adopted 3/10/94, Section 10)
Sec. 11.911 Civil Penalties
Any user or hauler who is found to have violated an order of the city council or who willfully or negligently failed
to comply with any provision of this Ordinance, and the orders, rules, regulations and permits issued hereunder,
shall be fined in accordance with the general penalty provision found in Section 1.106 of this code. In addition
to the penalties provided herein, the city may recover reasonable attorney's fees and other expenses of
litigation by appropriate suit at law against the person found to have violated this Ordinance or the orders, rules,
regulations and permits issued hereunder. Additional recoveries and relief in law and/or equity under existing
Federal or State law are precluded by specific recoveries obtained by the city under this section of the article.
(Ordinance 94-1 adopted 3/10/94, Section 11)
Sec. 11.912 Fees
It is the purpose of this section to provide for the recovery of costs from users of the city's wastewater disposal
system for the implementation of the program established herein. Fees shall be as provided for in the fee
schedule found in the appendix of this code. (Ordinance 94-1 adopted 3/10/94, Section 12)
ARTICLE 11.1000 WASTEWATER TREATMENT AND TRANSPORTATION USER CHARGE SYSTEM*
Sec. 11.1001 Requirements
The City of Seymour, as a recipient of a federal grant for the replacement and expansion of the wastewater
treatment and transportation facility, is required to develop and enact a user charge system to fairly distribute
the annual operation, maintenance and replacement costs of these facilities among all users and/or user
classes. (Ordinance 90-11 adopted 9/17/90, Section 1)
Sec. 11.1002 Definitions
BOD (Biochemical Oxygen Demand) means the quantity of oxygen utilized in the biochemical oxidation of
organic matter under standard laboratory procedures in five (5) days at 20°C, expressed in parts per million by
weight, or milligram per liter (mg/l).
Conventional Pollutant means those pollutants that are generally biodegradable and readily handled within
normal concentration ranges by conventional treatment processes. Conventional pollutants specifically include
biochemical oxygen demand, total suspended solids, fecal coliform, pH, oil, and grease.
Domestic Wastewater means the liquid waste normally originating in quarters inhabited or frequented by human
beings and may include human excreta, bath water, kitchen wastes (with or without properly shredded
garbage), and laundry waste.
Industrial Users means any nongovernmental, nonresidential user of a publicly owned treatment work which
discharges more than the equivalent of 25,000 gallons per day of sanitary wastes as defined in 40 CFR 35 of
Federal Rules and Regulations.
Non-conventional Pollutants means all other pollutants which are not specifically identified as either
conventional or toxic and includes such pollutants as chemical oxygen demand (COD), phosphorus, sulfates,
chlorides, etc.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 151/221
Non-residential Customers means all other customers receiving wastewater service and includes, but is not
limited to, commercial establishments, churches, schools, nursing homes, and hospitals.
Normal Wastewater Concentrations means wastewater having characteristics generally associated with typical
domestic wastewater and shall have the following limits:
BOD, 5 days @ 20°C 300 mg/l (max.)
Chlorine Demand 15 Min. 68°F 25 mg/l (max.)
Suspended Solids 300 mg/l (max.)
Hydrogen ion Concentration (pH) 5.0 to 9.0
Free Oil and Grease 10 mg/l (max.)
Oil and Grease, Total 100 mg/l (max.)
Temperature 125°F (max.)
NH3-N 30 mg/l (max.)
Objectionable Pollutant means those toxic and non-conventional pollutant causing an increase in the cost of
managing the effluent or sludge of the treatment waste. Suggested maximum limits for some objectional
pollutants are defined in the Sewer Use Ordinance.
Operation and Maintenance (O&M) Costs means those costs associated with the necessary operational
requirements of a wastewater treatment facility and collection system including replacement.
pH means the logarithm of the reciprocal of the weight of hydrogen ions in moles per liter of solution.
Prohibited Pollutants means any toxic or non-conventional pollutants that would cause problems in the
adequate treatment of the wastewater and would be required to be removed prior to any discharge into the
wastewater system.
Replacement means expenditures for obtaining and installing equipment, accessories, or appurtenances which
are necessary to maintain the capacity and performance of the treatment works during its service life.
Residential Customers means those customers living in homes, apartments, town houses, and trailers.
Sewer Superintendent means the person duly designated by the governing authority to oversee and supervise
the activities incident to the operation and maintenance of the sewage works, or his authorized deputy, agency
or representative.
Suspended Solids shall mean solids that either float on the surface of or are in suspension in water, sewage or
other liquids and which are removable by laboratory filtering.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 152/221
Toxic Pollutants means those pollutants which have been designated as toxic under Section 307 of the 1977
Clean Water Act, including all additions to the list.
User Charge means a charge levied on users of a treatment works for the user's proportionate share of the cost
of operation and maintenance of such works.
Other Terms. Terms not otherwise defined herein shall be as adopted in the latest edition of Standard Methods
for the Examination of Water and Wastewater, published by the American Public Health Association, the
American Water Works Association and the Water Pollution Control Federation.
(Ordinance 90-11 adopted 9/17/90, Section 2)
Sec. 11.1003 User Charges
(a) Customers with Normal Wastewater Contributions. In cases where wastewater characteristics contributed
by users are below or near the normal wastewater concentrations and do not contain any objectionable
pollutants, the user's charges are to be based on their estimated volume contribution.
(b) User Charge Formula. The individual customer charges will be based on the following formula:
Cu = Cb + (Ct/Vt) Vu
Where:
Cu = A user's monthly charge for wastewater service.
Cb = A user's share of monthly costs not related to operation and maintenance of wastewater
collection and treatment system.
Ct = Total operation and maintenance of lift stations and wastewater treatment facilities.
Vt = Total annual volume contribution from all users. Vt is the total annual volume of wastewater
received by the treatment facility. For the first year of operation of the plant, 0.257 million gallons per
day flow will be used. At the end of the first year, the actual flow measured at the plant shall be used.
Vu = The average monthly quantity of wastewater discharged by the individual user during winter
months. Average winter month's wastewater contribution is the average of the water consumed as
reflected on the user's water meter for the months of January, February, and March.
(Ordinance 90-11 adopted 9/17/90, Section 3.1)
Sec. 11.1004 Surcharge for Excessive Pollutant Concentrations
(a) Determination of Excessive Pollutant Concentrations. The superintendent of sewers will be responsible
for determining which users have sewage with excessive pollutant concentrations. Users who have effluent that
exceeds normal loading are responsible for self monitoring. The superintendent will determine the users who
are liable for surcharges either by individual testing or by using industry standards. If a user disputes his
surcharge, the burden of proof will be upon the user to show that his effluent meets normal loading
characteristics.
(b) Conventional Pollutants. In the event that conventional pollutant concentrations from a user exceed the
normal range of strength of domestic wastewater, a surcharge shall be levied. The use of such a surcharge
would be necessary if a user discharging a wastewater has a higher range of strength, and is located within the
city, and desires to have wastewater treatment service. The surcharge would be levied by the following formula:
Cs = (Bc(b) + Sc(s)) x Vu
where Cs = Surcharge for sewage of excessive strength.
Bc = O&M cost for treatment of a unit of BOD.
b = Concentration of BOD from a user above a base level of 300 mg/l.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 153/221
Sc = O&M cost for treatment of a unit of suspended solids (SS).
s = Concentration of SS from a user above a base level of 300 mg/l.
Vu = Volume concentration from a user per unit of time.
(c) Non-Conventional Pollutants. In the event that objectional pollutants or other non-conventional pollutants
are discharged into the system and cause an increase in the cost of managing the effluent or sludge of the
treatment works, the city shall take action to determine such cost and levee a surcharge to that user.
(Ordinance 90-11 adopted 9/17/90, Section 3.2)
Sec. 11.1005 User Charge Policy Requirements
(a) General Requirements. The user charge system shall be revised accordingly to accomplish the following:
(1) Maintain the proportionate distribution of operation and maintenance costs among the users
and user classes as required herein;
(2) Generate sufficient revenue to pay the total operation and maintenance cost necessary for the
proper operation and maintenance (including replacement) of the treatment and collection system
works; and
(3) Apply excess revenues collected from users or a class of users to the costs and operation and
maintenance fund, and adjust the rate accordingly in the following year.
(b) Review Period. It shall be the policy of the City of Seymour to review the User Charge System not less
than every year to insure that the general requirements of subsection (a) are met. It also shall be the policy of
the City of Seymour to review all user rate structures not less than every year to insure a fair distribution of
costs. After the first year of operation and enactment of this article, the City of Seymour shall review the User
Charge System annually and make the appropriate modifications.
(c) Notification. It shall be the policy of the City of Seymour that each user be notified at least annually in
conjunction with a regular bill of the sewer rate and that portion of the sewer bill which is attributable to the
Operation & Maintenance of the wastewater treatment and collection facilities.
(d) Complaints. It shall be the policy of the city to formally review complaints of sewer charges to a user at
any regularly scheduled city council meeting upon adequate notice.
(Ordinance 90-11 adopted 9/17/90, Section 4)
ARTICLE 11.1100 BULK WATER SALES
(a) The city shall, after the passage of this article, provide at least two racks to be used for the sale or
purchase of bulk water within the city.
(b) One of said racks shall be clearly designated in such a manner as to apprise the public that water sold
from said rack is to be used for human consumption; the second of said racks shall be clearly designated to
apprise the public that water sold from said rack shall not be used for human consumption.
(c) It shall be unlawful for any person, firm, corporation or institution to purchase water from the rack
designated as being for human consumption for any purpose other than for human or household use, or to use
said rack to fill any unsanitary or dangerous container.
(d) Any person, firm, corporation or institution found to be in violation of the terms of this article may be fined
in the municipal court of the city in accordance with the general penalty provision found in Section 1.106 of this
code, and additionally may be ordered to make full and complete restitution to the city for any damage done to
the water rack of the city and all equipment appurtenant thereto. In such even, not only will the individual
involved be charged with said offense, but said individual's employer, as well.
(Ordinance 91-3 adopted 5/9/91)
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 154/221
ARTICLE 11.1200 PROVISION OF UTILITIES TO NEW INDUSTRY
Sec. 11.1201 Service Free for Certain Periods
(a) Water, sewer and solid waste monthly services shall be provided free to new industry with five (5) to ten
(10) employees for a period of two (2) years.
(b) Water, sewer and solid waste monthly services shall be provided free to new industry with eleven (11) to
fifteen (15) employees for a period of three (3) years.
(c) Water, sewer and solid waste monthly services shall be provided free to new industry with fifteen (15) or
more employees for a period of five (5) years.
(Ordinance 92-7 adopted 8/13/92, Section 1)
Sec. 11.1202 Normal Usage Required
Section 11.1201 will apply only in cases of normal usage of water, sewer and solid waste services, as
determined by the city. (Ordinance 92-7 adopted 8/13/92, Section 2)
Sec. 11.1203 Determining Number of Employees
Employee numbers are determined by full time payroll employees on a yearly average number. (Ordinance 92-
7 adopted 8/13/92, Section 3)
Sec. 11.1204 Charges Resume upon Expiration of Period
After provisions of Section 11.1201 expires charges for water, sewer and solid waste services for present and
future industries located outside the city limits shall be the same as those located within the city limits.
(Ordinance 92-7 adopted 8/13/92, Section 4)
Sec. 11.1205 Industry Defined
Industry shall be defined as the manufacture of a product or service of a product that is destined for retail sale
in a large trade area. (Ordinance 92-7 adopted 8/13/92, Section 5)
ARTICLE 11.1300 INDUSTRIAL WASTE*
Sec. 11.1301 Definitions
Approving Authority means the city administrator or his duly authorized representative.
BOD (Biochemical Oxygen Demand) means the quantity of oxygen by weight, expressed in mg/l, utilized in the
biochemical oxidation of organic matter under standard laboratory conditions for five (5) days at a temperature
of twenty (20) degrees centigrade.
Building Sewer means the extension from the building drain to the public sewer on other place of disposal (also
called the house lateral and house connection).
City means the City of Seymour, County of Baylor, State of Texas, or any authorized person acting in its behalf.
COD (Chemical Oxygen Demand) means measure of the oxygen consuming capacity of inorganic and organic
matter present in the water or wastewater expressed in mg/l as the amount of oxygen consumed from a
chemical oxidant in a specific test, but not differentiating between stable and unstable organic matter and thus
not necessarily correlating with biochemical oxygen demand.
Control Manhole means a manhole giving access to a building sewer at some point before the building sewer
discharge mixes with other discharges in the public sewer.
Control Point means point of access to a course of discharge before the discharge mixes with other discharges
in the public sewer.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 155/221
Garbage means animal and vegetable wastes and residue from preparation, cooking and dispensing of food;
and from the handling, processing, storage and sale of food products and produce.
Industrial Waste means waste resulting from any process of industry, manufacturing, trade, or business from
the development of any natural resource, or any mixture of the waste with water or normal wastewater, or
distinct from normal wastewater.
Industrial Waste Charge means the charge made on those persons who discharge industrial wastes into the
city's sewerage system.
Milligrams Per Liter (mg/l) means the same as parts per million and is a weight-to-volume ratio; the milligramper-
liter value multiplied by the factor 8.34 shall be equivalent to pounds per million gallons of water.
Natural Outlet means any outlet into a watercourse, ditch, lake, or other body of surface water or groundwater.
Normal Domestic Wastewater means wastewater excluding industrial wastewater discharged by a person into
sanitary sewers and in which the average concentration of total suspended solids is not more than 300 mg/l
and BOD is not more than 300 mg/l.
Overload means the imposition of organic or hydraulic loading on a treatment facility in excess of its engineered
design capacity.
Person means any individual and includes any corporation, organization, government or governmental
subdivision or agency, business trust, estate, trust, partnership association, or other legal entity.
pH means the logarithm (Base 10) of the reciprocal of the hydrogen ion concentration.
Public Sewer means pipe or conduit carrying wastewater or unpolluted drainage in which owners of abutting
properties shall have the use, subject to control by the City of Seymour, Texas.
Sanitary Sewer means a public sewer that conveys domestic wastewater or industrial wastes or a combination
of both, and into which storm water, surface water, groundwater, and other unpolluted wastes are not
intentionally passed.
Slug means any discharge of water, wastewater or industrial waste which in concentration of any given
constituent or in quantity of flow, exceeds for any period of duration longer than fifteen (15) minutes more than
five (5) times the average twenty-four hour concentration or flows during normal operation.
Standard Methods means the examination and analytical procedures set forth in the latest edition, at the time of
analysis, of “Standard Methods for the Examination of Water and Wastewater” as prepared, approved, and
published jointly by the American Public Health Association, the American Water Works Association, and the
Water Pollution Control Federation.
Storm Sewer means a public sewer which carries storm and surface waters and drainage and into which
domestic wastewater or industrial wastes are not intentionally passed.
Storm Water means rainfall or any other forms of precipitation.
Superintendent means the Water and Wastewater Superintendent of the City of Seymour, Texas or his duly
authorized deputy, agent or representative.
Suspended Solids (SS) means solids measured in mg/l that either float on the surface of, or are in suspension
in, water, wastewater, or other liquids, and which are largely, removable by a laboratory filtration device.
To Discharge includes to deposit, conduct, drain, emit, throw, run, allow to seep, or otherwise release or
dispose of, or to allow, permit, or suffer any of these acts or omissions.
Trap means a device designed to skim, settle, or otherwise remove grease, oil, sand, flammable wastes or
other harmful substances.
Unpolluted Wastewater means water containing
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 156/221
(1) no free or emulsified grease or oil;
(2) no acids or alkalis;
(3) no phenols or other substances producing taste or odor in receiving water,
(4) no toxic or poisonous substances in suspension, colloidal state, or solution;
(5) no noxious or otherwise obnoxious or odorous gases;
(6) not more than an insignificant amount in mg/l each of suspended solids and BOD, as
determined by the Texas Water Commission; and
(7) color not exceeding fifty (50) units as measured by the Platinum-Cobalt method of
determination as specified in Standard Methods.
Waste means rejected, unutilized or superfluous substances in liquid, gaseous, or solid form resulting from
domestic, agricultural, or industrial activities.
Wastewater means a combination of the water-carried waste from residences, business buildings, institutions,
and industrial establishments, together with any ground, surface, and storm water that may be present.
Wastewater Facilities includes all facilities for collection, pumping, treating, and disposing of wastewater and
industrial wastes.
Wastewater Treatment Plant means any city-owned facilities, devices, and structures used for receiving,
processing and treating wastewater, industrial waste, and sludges from the sanitary sewers.
Wastewater Service Charge means the charge on all users of the public sewer system whose wastes do not
exceed in strength the concentration values established as representative of normal wastewater. and
Watercourse means a natural or man-made channel in which a flow of water occurs, either continuously or
intermittently.
(Ordinance 90-12 adopted 9/17/90, Section 1)
Sec. 11.1302 Prohibited Discharges
(a) No person may discharge to public sewers any waste which by itself or by interaction with other wastes
may
(1) injure or interfere with wastewater treatment processes or facilities.
(2) constitute a hazard to humans or animals; or
(3) create a hazard in receiving waters of the wastewater treatment plant effluent.
(b) All discharges shall conform to requirements of this article.
(Ordinance 90-12 adopted 9/17/90, Section 2)
Sec. 11.1303 Chemical Discharges
(a) No discharge to public sewers may contain:
(1) cyanide greater than 1.0 mg/l.
(2) fluoride other than that contained in the public water supply.
(3) chlorides in concentrations greater than 250 mg/l.
(4) gasoline, benzene, naphtha, fuel oil, or other flammable or explosive liquid, solid or gas; or
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 157/221
(5) substances causing an excessive Chemical Oxygen Demand (C.O.D.)
(b) No waste or wastewater discharged to public waters may contain:
(1) strong acid, iron pickling wastes, or concentrated plating solutions whether neutralized or not.
(2) fats, wax, grease, or oils, whether emulsified or not, in excess of one hundred (100) mg/l or
containing substances which may solidify or become viscous at temperature between thirty-two (32)
and one hundred fifty (150) degrees Fahrenheit (0 to 65 degrees Centigrade).
(3) objectionable or toxic substances, exerting an excessive chlorine requirement, to such degree
that any such material received in the composite wastewater treatment works exceeds the limits
established by the Approving Authority for such materials; or
(4) obnoxious, toxic or poisonous solids, liquids, or gases in quantities sufficient to violate the
provisions of subsection (a).
(c) No waste, wastewater, or other substance may be discharged into public sewers which has a pH lower
than 5.5 or higher than 9.5, or any other corrosive property capable of causing damage or hazard to structures,
equipment, and/or personnel at the wastewater facilities.
(d) All waste, wastewater, or other substance containing phenols, hydrogen sulfide, or other taste-and-odor
producing substances, shall conform to concentration limits established by the Approving Authority. After
treatment of the composite wastewater, concentration limits may not exceed the requirements established by
state, federal, or other agencies with jurisdiction over discharges to receiving waters.
(Ordinance 90-12 adopted 9/17/90, Section 3)

(a) No discharges may contain concentrations of hazardous metals other than amounts specified in Section
11.402(b).

Sec. 11.1305 Particulate Size
(a) No person may discharge garbage or other solids into public sewers unless it is shredded to a degree
that all particles can be carried freely under the flow conditions normally prevailing in public sewers. Particles
greater than one-half (1/2) inch in any dimensions are prohibited.
(b) The Approving Authority is entitled to review and approve the installation and operation of any garbage
grinder equipped with a motor of three-fourths (3/4) horsepower (0.76 hp metric) or greater.
(Ordinance 90-12 adopted 9/17/90, Section 5)
Sec. 11.1306 Storm Water and Other Unpolluted Drainage
(a) No person may discharge to public sanitary sewers:
(1) unpolluted storm water, surface water, groundwater, roof runoff or subsurface drainage.
(2) unpolluted cooling water.
(3) unpolluted industrial process waters.
(4) other unpolluted drainage.
or make any connection from inflow sources.
(b) In compliance with the Texas Water Quality Act and other statutes, the Approving Authority may
designate storm sewers and other watercourses into which unpolluted drainage described in subsection (a) of
this section may be discharged.
(Ordinance 90-12 adopted 9/17/90, Section 6)
Sec. 11.1307 Temperature
No person may discharge liquid or vapor having a temperature higher than one hundred fifty (150) degrees
Fahrenheit (65 degrees Centigrade), or any substance which causes the temperature to the total wastewater
treatment plant influent to increase at a rate of ten (10) degrees Fahrenheit or more per hour, or a combined
total increase of plant influent to one hundred ten (110) degrees Fahrenheit. (Ordinance 90-12 adopted 9/17/90,
Section 7)
Sec. 11.1308 Radioactive Wastes
(a) No person may discharge radioactive wastes or isotopes into public sewers without the permission of the
Approving Authority.
(b) The Approving Authority may establish, in compliance with applicable state and federal regulations,
regulations for discharge of radioactive wastes into public sewers.
(Ordinance 90-12 adopted 9/17/90, Section 8)
Sec. 11.1309 Impairment of Facilities
(a) No person may discharge into public sewers any substance capable of causing
(1) obstruction to the flow in sewers.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 160/221
(2) interference with the operation of treatment processes of facilities; or
(3) excessive loading of treatment facilities.
(b) Discharges prohibited by subsection (a) include, but are not limited to, materials which exert or cause
concentrations of
(1) inert suspended solids greater than 250 mg/l including but not limited to:
(A) Fuller's earth
(B) lime slurries; and
(C) lime residues.
(2) dissolved solids greater than 250 mg/l including but not limited to
(A) sodium chloride; and
(B) sodium sulfate.
(3) excessive discoloration including but not limited to
(A) dye wastes; and
(B) vegetable tanning solutions; or
(4) BOD, COD, or chlorine demand in excess of normal plant capacity.
(c) No person may discharge into public sewers any substance that may
(1) deposit grease or oil in the sewer lines in such a manner as to clog the sewers.
(2) overload skimming and grease handling equipment.
(3) pass to the receiving waters without being effectively treated by normal wastewater treatment
processes due to the nonamenability of the substance to bacterial action: or
(4) deleteriously affect the treatment process due to excessive quantities.
(d) No person may discharge any substance into public sewers which
(1) is not amenable to treatment or reduction by the processes and facilities employed; or
(2) is amenable to treatment only to such a degree that the treatment plant effluent cannot meet
the requirements of other agencies having jurisdiction over discharge to the receiving waters.
(e) The Approving Authority shall regulate the flow and concentration of slugs when they may:
(1) impair the treatment process;
(2) cause damage to collection facilities;
(3) incur treatment costs exceeding those for normal wastewater, or
(4) render the effluent unfit for stream disposal or industrial use.
(f) No person may discharge into public sewers solid or viscous substances which may violate subsection (a)
section if present in sufficient quantity or size including but not limited to:
(1) ashes;
(2) cinders;
